All Factories and Shops in This City Should Strictly Implement Labor Vocational Education - The Social Bureau and Literacy Education Association Jointly Issue a Notice Requiring Submission of Lists of Literate and Illiterate Workers by a Deadline 97

According to the Shanghai News Agency, in order to promote literacy education for workers, the municipal government previously promulgated the "Implementation Measures for Labor Literacy Education," and the Literacy Education Committee immediately issued "Guidelines for Factories and Shops to Establish Labor Literacy Schools" to facilitate compliance. The Literacy Education Committee held a joint meeting of district directors yesterday to discuss the measures and jointly issued a notice with the Social Bureau, ordering all factories and shops to submit lists of literate and illiterate workers. The details are as follows:

Joint Notice

The Social Bureau and Literacy Education Committee jointly issued a notice stating that the "Implementation Measures for Labor Literacy Education" in this city have been promulgated and implemented by the municipal government. All illiterate workers within the city should receive literacy education. Those who have graduated from school and hold certificates, or who can recognize the 600-character list prescribed by the association, must be examined and verified to be considered literate workers and exempt from literacy education. The aforementioned workers should report to their employers by the 20th of this month and submit their certificates. All factories and shops must prepare lists of workers requesting exemption from literacy education and illiterate workers, along with the certificates submitted by literate workers, and submit them to the association's district offices for verification by the 10th of this month. Workers who fail to report by the deadline will be considered illiterate and will be forced to receive literacy education. If factories and shops fail to report by the deadline, they will be fined up to 20 yuan upon discovery and will still be ordered to submit the lists by a deadline. Blank lists can be obtained from the association's district offices nearby. All should comply. This notice is hereby issued. Chairman Wu Tiecheng, Vice-Chairman Pan Gongzhan, Director Yu Xingya.

Joint Meeting

The Literacy Education Committee convened a joint meeting of office directors at the association's office at 2:00 PM yesterday to provide instructions on labor literacy education matters. Present were the association's Secretary-General Tao Baichuan, Director of the Labor Education Section Wang Gang, and district directors Lu Hailan, Jiang Menglin, Chen Songchun, Jiang Wenbao, and others, totaling more than 20 people. After Chairman Tao Baichuan performed the opening ceremony, the chairman reported on the "Implementation Measures for Labor Literacy Education." Subsequently, the following important matters were resolved: (1) Any areas within the jurisdiction of the district offices that have not yet been surveyed must be surveyed by July 30th and reported to the association by August 10th. (2) Factories with fewer than 100 employees will be the responsibility of the district offices to encourage and guide the establishment of labor literacy schools, or to transfer illiterate workers to various literacy schools. (3) Factories with more than 100 employees will be the responsibility of the Social Bureau to encourage and guide the establishment of labor literacy schools, but after the literacy schools are established, they will still be handed over to the district offices for management.

Progress on the Yangtze River Pooling Agreement is Smooth - Expected to be Implemented on August 1st 101

The Yangtze River Six Companies' Pooling Agreement previously encountered obstacles due to the Nissin Company's proposal to increase its business share, leading to repeated postponements. It was learned yesterday that the Nissin authorities no longer insist on the pooling percentage, the obstacles have been removed, and progress is smooth. Preparations such as inspecting ships have begun. The details are as follows:

Nissin Company's Sympathy

Previously, the Nissin Company felt that it would be at a disadvantage if it joined the pooling agreement, as its cargo transportation on the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, such as the Hankou-Yichang route, was more prosperous than that of other companies. After discussions among the five shipping companies, it was agreed with the Nissin authorities that the pooling agreement would be based on the overall business, and there would be both advantages and disadvantages. Therefore, the transshipment of British ships was also included in the pooling agreement. It is now understood that after several negotiations, Nissin has understood the situation, and there are no obstacles to the progress.

Rushing to Complete Procedures

The second postponement was originally intended to take effect yesterday to facilitate the six companies' calculation of the pooling percentages. However, the six companies have a total of 65 Yangtze River ships within the pooling range, with a total tonnage of over 170,000, and 88 barges, also reaching about 200,000 tons. The first step in implementing the pooling agreement is to inspect all Yangtze River ships and barges to determine the recognized tonnage, which will be used as the standard for calculating the percentages in the future. However, due to the large number of ships and barges, and the fact that they are not all in one place, the inspection can only be carried out in batches. Yesterday, the six companies held another meeting to rush preparations such as ship inspections and decided to start soon.

Implementation Date

Since it was not possible to implement the pooling agreement yesterday, the six companies had already telegraphed the various companies in Yichang, Hankou, Jiujiang, Anqing, and Wuhu for information. The third scheduled implementation date is the 22nd. However, a reporter from this newspaper spoke to a representative of the six companies yesterday, who said that there were no other issues with the pooling agreement itself. The current discussions are only about the complexity of the various procedures. It is difficult to say whether the ship inspection and tonnage determination can be completed by the 22nd. The feasibility of implementing it on the 22nd is still uncertain. It is likely that the implementation date will be around August 2nd.

Lawyers Association Suggests That Court Hearings Can Be Postponed 102

The Shanghai Lawyers Association yesterday suggested to the various levels of courts in the city that if scheduled court hearings cannot be held on time, postponements should be allowed. The written submission stated: "Regarding the suggestion that if scheduled court hearings cannot be held on time, postponements should be allowed, according to a proposal by member Xu Zuoliang, the courts in Shanghai are now conducting trials according to the New Life Movement, and all trials are conducted on time. However, in practice, judges and lawyers still inevitably encounter obstacles. (1) From the judge's perspective, for example, Case A is scheduled for 10:00 AM, Case B is scheduled for 10:30 AM, and Case C is scheduled for 11:00 AM. They are tried in order. If Case A is complicated and needs to be extended by an hour, if the judge takes into account Cases B and C, then Case A will inevitably be handled hastily. If the judge handles the case in detail, it will have to be extended and Cases B and C will be delayed. This is one difficulty. (2) From the lawyer's perspective, lawyers in Shanghai currently practice in five courts, including the High Court and the local courts. Court hearings are scheduled to begin at 10:00 AM in one court and at 11:00 AM in the local court, with a difference of one hour. Since there is no time conflict, they can be handled concurrently, and there is no need to appoint a sub-agent. If the judge encounters a complicated case and the trial is extended by one or two hours, or if the judge takes temporary leave, the acting judge may postpone the trial due to the sudden increase in cases. In this situation, lawyers are often unaware of the cause and wait quietly for a summons, wasting one or two hours, which is common. Cases that could have been handled concurrently due to the lack of time conflict end up being missed. It is difficult to achieve both. Furthermore, both Cases A and B may not be able to be handled in court. For example, if Case A is postponed due to the judge taking leave, and the lawyer rushes to Case B, they will have already missed the deadline. The client often thinks that the lawyer is not doing their job properly, but the lawyer is in a difficult situation. This is the second difficulty. In my humble opinion, if the court cannot hold a hearing on time, the lawyer should be allowed to request a postponement of one or two hours, or one or two days, to avoid inconvenience for both parties. The association submitted this to the 199th joint meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committees, and it was resolved that member Xu's proposal was not without merit and should be forwarded to the court to request adoption and implementation. In addition to submitting it separately, we hereby submit this document to request that your court review, adopt, and implement it for the public good."

Niu Weisi, the Party Affairs Instructor of the Second District of Jiangsu Province, believes that the New Life Movement should not be limited to urban areas. Charity Organizations and the Public Security Bureau Separately Send Away Large Numbers of Refugees - 134 People Take a Steamer Back to Their Hometowns, and 250 People Take a Train to Hangzhou 104

Recently, the number of refugees from various counties outside the province coming to Shanghai and begging on the streets has been increasing daily. Every day, large numbers of refugees gather at the Xinwei Relief Association of the Renji Hall on Yunnan Road in the Public Concession, and over 3,000 refugees have already been sent back. However, yesterday, under the scorching sun, a large number of refugees went to the association to request to be sent back to their hometowns by steamer, including 41 from Wuhu, 49 from Anqing, 39 from Datong, 2 from Nanjing, and 3 from Hankou, totaling 134 men and women. After the clerk, Ge Yunsun, issued the tickets, the clerk Chen Youtang checked the number of people and escorted them to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Jiang'an steamer to be disembarked at the above-mentioned ports along the Yangtze River to return to their hometowns. Those taking a train to Hangzhou: Yesterday afternoon at about 5:00 PM, 250 refugees, men, women, and children from Xiping Township, arrived in Shanghai by steamer from Chongming. The refugee representatives, Sun Shaobin and Huang Zicheng, requested assistance from the Municipal Public Security Bureau. After receiving the report, Director Cai Jinjun immediately instructed Hong Qi, the chief of the Second Military Affairs Section, to send personnel to lead the refugees to the Jianding Guild Hall at the South Railway Station for accommodation. Food rations were also issued to each person. It is said that they will take a train to Hangzhou today (the 17th) to be sent back.

Measures for Handling Passengers Riding Trains Without Tickets - Ministry of Railways Orders Railway Bureaus to Comply 105

The Ministry of Railways yesterday instructed the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureaus: "According to the case presented by the Business Department, the 21st motion of the 9th National Railway Transportation Conference, proposed by the Jinpu Railway, requested supplementing Article 47 of the General Rules for Passenger Car Transportation. The conference resolved in the 40th resolution that passengers riding without tickets should be handed over to the railway police after being removed from the train. The General Rules should be supplemented accordingly." After verification, it is feasible. The sentence "has the right to remove them from the train" in the third paragraph of Article 47 (6) of the General Rules for Passenger Car Transportation should be supplemented with "After being removed from the train, they should be handed over to the railway police for leaving the station and not allowed to linger." This order is issued separately and must be complied with. It is understood that the railway bureau has already instructed the Transportation Department and the Police Department to comply with the order.

Local Indian Residents Donate to Quetta Earthquake Victims 109

This year, a severe earthquake occurred in Quetta, India, causing immense suffering. The Indian community in Shanghai felt deeply affected by this tragedy. Through the efforts of Indian personnel from the Shanghai Municipal Council Police Department and various prisons, a total of 845.50 Chinese dollars was raised. This amount, combined with the 250 Chinese dollars granted to the Indian Charity Fund in Shanghai to commemorate the 25th anniversary of the British Emperor's accession to the throne last month, brings the total to 1,095.50 Chinese dollars. All of this money has been handed over to Mr. Bailey, the British Consul-General in Shanghai, to be remitted to India for disaster relief.

Infrequent Rainfall in June Causes Fewer Park Visitors 110

According to a report from the Parks Department of the Shanghai Municipal Council, continuous rainfall in the latter half of June this year led to a decrease of 62,286 visitors in all parks compared to the same month last year. The total number of visitors to all parks this month was 380,229. Furthermore, due to the muddy and damp conditions at Hongkou Park, the sports grounds were closed for as many as seven days. Open-air concerts in various parks were canceled due to rain on ten occasions. The total number of musical performances this month was only ten military band performances and four orchestral performances. According to records from meteorological instruments at Jiaozhou Road Park, the total rainfall was 8.861 inches. The highest temperature was 92.3 degrees, the lowest was 61.2 degrees, the average highest was 82.5, and the average lowest was 68.4 degrees.

Steam Launch Cylinder Explodes, Injuring Chinese and Westerners 111

At around 11:00 AM yesterday, a steam launch on the Huangpu River, carrying one Westerner and two Chinese individuals, suddenly experienced a cylinder explosion. With a loud bang, scalding steam and debris scattered, injuring everyone on board. Upon hearing the news, the Customs immediately dispatched a rescue boat for assistance. An ambulance transported the Westerner to the Country Hospital, while the two Chinese were taken to Renji Hospital. The nationality, surname, and age of the Westerner are unknown. One of the Chinese men was named Wang Xiaodi, a local resident, aged 34, who was the captain of the launch. The other was Tang Bingjin, from Zhejiang, aged 29, who worked as a security guard. Fortunately, their injuries were minor, and they were discharged from the hospital after receiving treatment.

New Seaside Bathing Beach Opened at Qijiadun on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway - Boundless Sea and Sky, Myriad Phenomena - Nothing Surpasses It for Relaxation and Enjoyment - Opening Scheduled for July 21st 112

The Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway travels south from Minhang along the coast, with the Jinshanwei area protruding into the sea, where the waves are magnificent. At Qijiadun, the area forms a bay, with Jinshan and Zhapu mountains standing in the sea like natural emerald screens. The beauty of the scenery is unmatched in the suburbs of Shanghai. During this hot summer, the sea breeze is refreshing. Sitting and gazing into the distance, one sees a boundless sea and sky with myriad phenomena. Gulls skim the water, sails appear and disappear. Nothing surpasses it for relaxation and enjoyment. Moreover, the beach is flat, the sand is clean, the tide is gentle, the depth is moderate, the water contains salt, and the air is fresh, making it ideal for swimming and escaping the summer heat. It is only sixty miles from Shanghai, with direct car access since the highway was completed. Westerners have been flocking there to swim. However, there was a lack of adequate facilities to meet the needs of visitors. Local individuals, Zhang Zhongcai, Zhang Bolan, Zhang Mingguang, and others, passionate about community service, have utilized the surrounding scenery to develop a seaside bathing beach. Construction began this spring, incurring considerable expense. After half a year, it is now nearing completion. The bathing area covers over five hundred mu, vast and spacious, with grassy banks that are neat and charming. The interior buildings include rest rooms, changing rooms, a refreshment hall, fresh water rinsing rooms, and bedrooms, all well-proportioned and comfortable. Cold drinks, tea, and snacks are readily available. Water sports equipment, such as swimsuits, rowing boats, examples of canopy tents, and large umbrellas, are also well-equipped. It is rumored that the beach will be opened on July 21st, adding another scenic spot to the suburbs of Shanghai during the long summer.

Shanghai Was Stuffy and Hot Yesterday - Evening Brought No Wind - Horse Collapses from Heatstroke on Guling Road - Sudden Increase in Patients at the Isolation Hospital 113

Although there were strong winds and heavy rain in Shanghai the night before last, it was brief. Yesterday morning, the scorching sun was high in the sky, making the heat even more intense. The evening was even more stuffy, with no wind at all. People seeking relief from the heat on the streets were covered in sweat. Working in such conditions was unbearably difficult. Yesterday afternoon, around 3:00 PM, a carriage with city license number 117, Concession license number (English) 20, and (French) 24, was traveling to the intersection of Guling Road and Changsha Road when the horse suddenly collapsed from heatstroke. Despite the coachman's efforts to cool it with ice, it remained unable to stand until 8:00 PM. A reporter from the Datong News Agency also inquired by telephone with the Beixizang Road Emergency Isolation Hospital. The number of patients increased sharply yesterday, with 190 patients at the Shanghai Isolation Hospital and 345 patients at the Shanghai Epidemic Hospital.

Meeting Minutes of the Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Society 114

The board of directors of the Shanghai Municipal Council Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Society held its 20th meeting last Friday. Attendees included Mr. Massey (Chairman), Peng Jin, Yi Zitong, Zhu Maocheng, Gu Songmao, Xie Andao, and Tao Deman, among others. Statistical reports were presented, indicating that all aspects of the Mutual Aid Society's work were progressing well. For example, twenty-two tea stations have been established by the Society. The Medical Committee convened a meeting on June 24th, and its reports and recommendations have been approved by the board of directors. The minutes of the Personnel Committee meetings held on the 19th, 27th, and 28th of last month were also passed. The budget proposal for the next year was prepared by the Program Budget Committee and submitted to the board of directors for detailed discussion. As a result, the proposal was approved in principle, but the details still need to be compared and reviewed. Roughly speaking, the monthly income is approximately 14,885 yuan, while the expenditure is 13,703 yuan, leaving a surplus that can be used for unexpected needs. The main categories of expenditure are listed below:

Social insurance, relief, and medical care: 6,815 yuan, accounting for 50%

Administrative expenses: 3,300 yuan, 15%

Education and sports activities: 1,253 yuan, 8%

Bathing: 1,415 yuan, 10%

Tea and recreation: 440 yuan, 4%

Dormitory facilities: 310 yuan, 3%

Furthermore, the board of directors discussed in detail the livelihood issues of rickshaw pullers after the registration deadline. Once rickshaw puller registration becomes mandatory, how will those who fail to register be supported? The board of directors resolved to establish a separate "Special Relief Committee for Unregistered Rickshaw Pullers" and appointed Massey, Xie Andao, Zhu Maocheng, Wang Zhiren, and Peng Jin as committee members to conduct investigations and make recommendations. In addition, improvements were made to the implementation procedures of the Mutual Aid Society's education program. In the future, the children of rickshaw pullers, including adults, will not only be taught reading and writing but also handicrafts as a mandatory part of the curriculum. Mr. Chen Heqin from the Education Department was invited to assist with this matter. At the end of the meeting, Mr. Gu Songmao proposed that the Mutual Aid Society establish a free tire replacement station. Mr. Gu stated that the hot weather makes tires prone to bursting, and a free replacement station would save rickshaw pullers time. After discussion, the board of directors agreed that while this would greatly benefit the rickshaw pullers, the nature of the work falls within the rickshaw owners' responsibilities, and the Mutual Aid Society could not undertake such a significant responsibility. Furthermore, the three social workers of the board of directors had resigned. The board of directors approved the resignations and expressed its regret.

The Taxpayers Association Will Appeal Again for the Pushcart Industry - Continuing to Request the Shanghai Municipal Council to Cancel the Increased Levy - The Pushcart Industry Association Sends Letter Requesting Participation in the Protest 115

The Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers Association sent a letter yesterday to Mr. Philip, Acting Secretary-General of the Shanghai Municipal Council, stating: "Regarding the increased levy on pushcarts, we have already written to your bureau, based on facts and legal principles, requesting its cancellation. We have received a letter from the Shanghai Pushcart Industry Mutual Aid Association, which states: 'Our pushcart industry relies on physical strength to transport goods for customers, earning a meager income to make a living. The current Municipal Council's decision to double the levy on our industry during these difficult times has left us bewildered and shocked. Our members find it difficult to accept and dare to express our grievances as follows: (1) The cost of a pushcart is only about 20 yuan, but after the increase, the total annual levy will exceed the cost. If all types of freight vehicles on the market were subject to taxes exceeding their cost, what would that be? Why should our pushcarts be singled out for harsh treatment? (2) Since the emergence of trucks and other vehicles in the market, the scope of our pushcart industry has been narrowed by environmental pressures and is already struggling to survive. It is like a leaky house being hit by wind and rain. (3) Shanghai is an East Asian metropolis, and recently, it has been hit by the international economic recession, and frequent droughts and floods have led to rural bankruptcy, affecting all industries. The sharp decline in passenger and freight traffic has been particularly severe for our industry. (4) What all industries need today is rent and tax reductions. Only in this way can we sustain the precarious situation and avoid total collapse. Therefore, landlords are voluntarily reducing rents, and the authorities should also consider reducing levies to adapt to the situation and prevent unemployment from continuing to expand in order to ensure public order. The levy on our pushcart industry was originally 2.5 yuan per quarter, which was already considered heavy compared to other freight vehicles. How can we bear another increase? (5) In terms of vehicles meeting market needs, trucks are indeed fast for transporting goods. However, if there are not many goods, hiring a truck is economically impractical. Replacing them with ordinary small carts is too heavy and prone to tipping. Pushcarts are still the most suitable and stable choice, so the market cannot do without them. There is an objective reason for this. (6) It is estimated that there are more than 14,000 to 15,000 pushcarts in the city, and more than 100,000 people directly or indirectly rely on them for a living. Now, the increase in the levy will deprive them of their livelihoods, which will undoubtedly increase social unrest. In summary, considering the current situation and the special circumstances of our industry, we should be discussing tax reductions, not tax increases. We, the members, have no choice but to present our plight. We have long admired your association's understanding of the suffering of our laborers. We respectfully request you to lobby the Municipal Council to cancel the increased levy to ensure our livelihoods.' Representatives from the association came to the meeting and poured out their grievances, which brought tears to our eyes. Your bureau has doubled the levy on pushcarts, raising it to more than half of their cost. If it is only a matter of revenue, then we should implement the new method of collecting municipal general levies proposed by our association's general assembly of representatives. I am afraid that the increased amount will certainly be more than just 100,000 yuan per year. If it is out of consideration for the difficult times and we must stick to the old ways, then why must we burden the coolies who can barely earn enough to eat with the feeling of having nothing to look forward to, just for a new revenue of more than 100,000 yuan? The number of unemployed people in Shanghai is increasing daily, and the municipal authorities should provide relief, not exacerbate the situation. We strongly believe that the proposed increase in the levy should be cancelled immediately, so as to ensure their legitimate livelihoods. This is beneficial to both the public and private sectors. Sincerely, To Mr. Philip, Acting Secretary-General of the Shanghai Public Concession Municipal Council."

The Shanghai pushcart industry representatives Chen Xiaoming, Feng Taoyuan, and Wang Wenyuan, etc., specifically sent a letter to the pushcart industry mutual aid society to jointly protest the Municipal Council's increased levy, the original text of which reads: "Dear Sirs, We have learned that the Shanghai Public Concession Municipal Council's Transportation Department has, without considering the current difficult times, suddenly decided to increase the vehicle levy on our pushcarts amidst this economic downturn. Forced by the need to make a living, we have collectively decided to unanimously express our opposition and resolve to join your association to strengthen our collective power. We hereby write to you, and we have already sent a letter to the Chinese Taxpayers Association of the Concession requesting that it be handled together."

Weak Director of the Film Industry, Zheng Zhengqiu, Passes Away - Devoted to the Dramatic Arts in the Late Qing Dynasty - Later Founded Star Film Company, Directing 23 Famous Films 118

Mr. Zheng Zhengqiu, a pioneer in the Chinese film industry, suddenly passed away at 7:10 AM yesterday due to heart failure at his residence at No. 4 Anji Lane, Mu'erming Road, at the age of 48. In his early years, Mr. Zheng engaged in the New Drama movement. When the film industry arose, he turned his efforts to the development of domestic films. In addition to co-founding the Star Film Company with Zhang Shichuan, Zhou Jianyun, Dong Tianya, and others, and serving as its associate manager, he directed as many as 23 films. He also actively participated in public welfare activities, serving as the vice-chairman of the Guangdong Fellow Provincials Association, the chairman of the Chaozhou Fellow Provincials Association, and the president of Heji Hospital, among other positions. A reporter from the Central News Agency specifically visited to learn about Mr. Zheng's life and death, which are recorded below:

Plagued by Illness, He Suddenly Passed Away

Mr. Zheng had a weak constitution and was plagued by illness for many years. However, because he had great ambition for his career, he was able to release a new film every year. On the 8th of this month, when Zhou Jianyun and Hu Die returned to the country, Zheng still supported his illness to attend the welcome meeting at the Star Film Company and gave a loud speech. Unexpectedly, he would pass away in less than ten days. Zheng had been suffering from heart failure. Because he was the president of Heji Hospital, he immediately asked the Western and Chinese doctors in the hospital for diagnosis and treatment. From the 10th onwards, his condition gradually worsened. On the 11th, it became more severe and he could not speak. On the 13th and 14th, there was a slight improvement, but on the afternoon of the 15th, he finally reached a critical condition and fell into a coma. Yesterday morning, around 6:00 AM, Zhang Shichuan, Zhou Jianyun, and other colleagues from the Star Film Company were still comforting Mr. Zheng at his bedside. At 7:00 AM, he bid farewell forever. It was not expected that he would suddenly pass away within ten minutes. Mr. Zheng's body was transported to the Shanghai Funeral Home on Xujiahui Road at 9:30 AM yesterday morning. After being washed, it was placed in a coffin in the funeral parlor behind the hall. Colleagues from the Star Film Company and friends of Mr. Zheng came to offer condolences in an endless stream. Mr. Zheng is survived by his elderly mother, Madam Zhang, who is 75 years old, his wife, Yu Mengjun, who is 47 years old, three sons: Xiaoxiaoqiu, who is 24 years old, Erqiu, who is 18 years old, and You Sanqiu, who is 14 years old, and one daughter, Youqiu. Except for Xiaoxiaoqiu, who has been acting in the Star Film Company for many years, the rest are studying at the Minguo Junior Middle School. Mr. Zheng's funeral has been scheduled for 2:00 PM on the afternoon of the 18th.

Early Theatrical Life Was Rich

Mr. Zheng's original name was Bochang. He was the adopted son of Zheng Qiaji, a wealthy merchant from Chaozhou, Guangdong. As a child, he was taught by Mr. Zhuang Chenghuang (who once wrote editorials for the Zhonghua Minbao in the first and second years of the Republic of China). When he was a young man, he brought two million yuan from his mother to Shanghai to do business. However, he had a special interest in drama. During the reign of Emperor Xuantong in the late Qing Dynasty, when Mr. Yu Youren founded the Minhu Bao in Shanghai, he wrote theatrical criticism under the pen name Yaofeng. At that time, Xu Zhuodai and others were launching the New Drama movement. They invited him to watch Japanese plays in the Hongkou area, which greatly increased his interest. Within two years, the Asia Film Company founded by Zhang Shichuan failed. Zheng took over all of its personnel and formed the Xinmin New Drama Society, performing at the Lanxin Grand Theatre on Museum Road. He was skilled in both male and female roles. At first, it was not successful. Later, Zheng starred in plays about stepmothers abusing children, which were very popular with the audience. Then, he joined Zhang Shichuan in co-founding the Minming New Drama Society and the Xiaowu Stage. Later, he joined Zhang, Zhou, and others in co-founding the Star Film Company, devoting himself entirely to domestic films and serving as a director. When Zheng was young, he had small stones in his gallbladder. A German doctor found a way to crush them and excrete them in his urine. Because of the excessive pain, he developed a smoking habit. A few years ago, Zheng was also persuaded by the German Dr. Himit's theory of rejuvenating the elderly and underwent tests with Zheng Zhegu. Zhegu passed away within a year, and Zheng Zhengqiu's body became even weaker as a result. Even in summer, his hands were as cold as ice. Recently, Mr. Zheng was trying to quit smoking, but unexpectedly, his heart disease worsened and he suddenly passed away.

His Contribution to the Film Industry Is Significant

Over the past ten years, Mr. Zheng has directed 23 films at Star Film Company. Although some people criticized him for being overly influenced by the New Drama style, each film was a box office success. "Flower of Freedom", "Two Sisters", and "Rebirth Flower" were particularly popular. The Star Film Company relied on him to overcome economic difficulties many times. Recently, Zheng had written another play called "Brothers", which had not yet begun filming. Many people in the current film industry have been promoted by Zheng. He is commonly respected as "Old Master Zheng".

A List of Mr. Zheng's Directed Films

Little Lover, A Little Worker, Plum Blossom Falls, White Cloud Pagoda (the above two films were co-directed with Zhang Shichuan), Twenty-Eight Beauties, Tablet of Blood and Tears, Yang Xiaozhen, Black-Clad Female Knight (co-directed with Cheng Bugao), Female Knight Saves Her Husband, The First Part of Blood and Tears Yellow Flowers, The Second Part of Blood and Tears Yellow Flowers (the above two films were co-directed with Cheng Bugao), Beauty Under the Knife, Little Comrades in the War Zone, Broken Qin Tower, Peach Blossom Lake, Red Tears Shadow, Jade Beauty's Eternal Farewell, Spring Water Love Waves, Flower of Freedom, Two Sisters, Rebirth Flower, Daughter's Classic, Passionate Patriotic Soul (one film directed by Zheng), Brothers (written but not filmed)

Jiahe Steamer Crew Members Shen Qinxiang and Others Arrive in Shanghai - Li Xiaobin Died of Illness in the Pirate Den at the End of Last Year - Pirate Leader Hu Chun Captured by the Guangzhou Public Security Bureau 119

The state-owned China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Jiahe Steamer was robbed by pirates in Dapeng Bay between Xiamen and Shantou on November 4th last year, and three people, including the business director Shen Qinxiang, the accountant Ge Liangchen, and Li Xiaobin, were kidnapped. Record of the Opening Trial of the Great China Tragedy: Most of the Male and Female Victims, Young and Old, Appeared in Court; Judge Will Visit the Fire Site When Necessary; Judge Advises the Factory to Provide Hundreds of Yuan in Relief First 120

The Great China Celluloid Factory, located at No. 100, Lane 1371, Xiaoshadu Road, West Shanghai, specializes in manufacturing children's toys and ping-pong balls. Adjacent to it is Yongqing Lane, which is divided into ten alleys, mostly inhabited by commoners and workers. On the 28th of last month, at around 8 p.m., a fire suddenly broke out there, with flames reaching the sky and thick smoke billowing. The residents of Yongqing Lane scrambled to escape. As of now, twenty-six men and women have died from burns or other causes, and fifty-three others have been injured, marking an unprecedented disaster. Afterward,

the affected victims organized a disaster relief association, believing that the fire originated from the Great China Factory's warehouse. They hired lawyers Wang Weigu, Wei Weiqing, Sun Bawu, and others to represent forty family members of the victims, including Wu Shaowen, and filed a complaint with the First Special Court's Criminal Division, accusing the factory's manager Jiang Junyan, assistant manager and factory director Ge Tianmin, deputy factory director Qian Menglin, general manager Sun Hongcheng, chairman Zhu Rutang, and other five people of causing death through negligence and endangering public safety. Yesterday afternoon at 4:15 p.m., Judge Liu Yugui presided over the hearing in the Eighth Criminal Court. Due to the seriousness of the case,

many people from all walks of life came to observe. Most of the victims also appeared in court, including men, women, the old, and the young, all bearing scars. Except for Qian Menglin, the other five defendants, along with their defense lawyers Xu Jie, Ling Qihong, and Gu Yongquan, appeared in court to respond to the charges. The Public Concession police authorities also considered this case important, so in addition to sending Western officers to court to record the statements of all parties, and to ensure thorough security and prevent accidents, the District Chief of District C, a Westerner named Kai Naina, and Chief Inspector Wu Genyuan personally supervised a large number of detectives and police officers inside and outside the court, together with the original bailiffs,

to maintain order. Judge Liu, noting the large number of plaintiffs, ordered the election of several representatives to testify. The victims then elected Wu Shaowen, Zhou Degan, Liu Songshou, and other three people as representatives. Wu Shaowen, from Jiangbei, residing in the Eighth Alley of Yongqing Lane, stated that his home was not far from the Great China Factory of the defendants, separated only by a small alley. On August 1st of last year, the factory had a fire once before. Afterward, we, in the name of all the tenants, commissioned lawyer Wang to send a letter to the factory, requesting the demolition of the fence and the repair of the firewalls. Although they promised to repair them at the time,

no action was taken. Unexpectedly, on June 28th of this year, at around 8 p.m., the factory caught fire again. The fire started in the factory's storage room, which was filled with explosive materials. With a thunderous sound, the fire spread rapidly and violently, engulfing Alleys 6, 7, 8, 9, and 10 of Yongqing Lane where we lived. At that time, I was cooling off when I saw the fire. Because there was no back door and the fire was extremely hot and fast, everyone climbed over the wall to the small alley and desperately escaped through the flames. Those who couldn't escape were buried in the fire pit. In this disaster,

thirteen houses were destroyed. Because they were all commoners, each house housed several families, so about twenty-seven families were affected. Twenty-six men and women were burned to death, and thirty were hospitalized for injuries. Besides my entire family being destroyed, five people were burned to death, and now only I am left, he said, tears streaming down his face, pleading for justice. Zhou Degan and Liu Songshou testified that four members of their families each were burned to death, and two members of Liu's family were seriously injured and are still in the hospital. The rest of their testimony was similar to Wu Shaowen's, so it was omitted. Questioned, defendant

Jiang Junyan testified that he was the manager of the Dahua Celluloid Factory. The factory was separated from Yongqing Lane by a small alley to the west, with no brick wall, only a fence. Although there was a fire once on August 1st of last year, he did not receive a letter from the tenants of Yongqing Lane requesting the construction of a wall afterward. Furthermore, all matters in the factory were the responsibility of the factory director, he said. Ge Tianmin testified that he was the factory director of the Great China Factory. If there were important matters, he would report them to the general manager, who would then report them to the board of directors for approval. During the fire last year, he was not at the factory, so the former factory director Qian Zhenghua was in charge. The Qian Menglin accused by the plaintiffs was not an employee of our factory, so he was completely unaware of the plaintiffs'

requests for wall construction. He investigated that the Great China Factory was not the site of the fire, because the raw material warehouse in our factory was closed and locked every day after 6 p.m. and had no electric lights, so how could it have caught fire? Therefore, our factory was also one of those burned. Furthermore, according to outside rumors, the fire came from Yongqing Lane, but I cannot provide evidence for this claim; it is just hearsay. Judge Liu said that the court had inspected the Great China Factory yesterday while conducting an on-site investigation in West Shanghai for another case, and saw the

fire originating from the factory's warehouse. Ge replied, It was not our factory that caught fire, because our factory has 170-180 male and female workers. In this disaster, besides the warehouse being destroyed, the roof of the furnace room was also burned. The room uses coal to generate steam and has two workers dedicated to it, who start work at 5 a.m. and stop at 5:30 p.m. The warehouse is about thirty feet away from the furnace room. Currently, due to the damage to the machinery in the factory after the fire, work has been suspended. However, according to outside rumors, this fire actually started from the Seventh Alley of Yongqing Lane. As for the cause of the fire, it is said that it was due to using a blowtorch

to cook supper carelessly, causing sparks to spread to the toilet and then to the warehouse, he said. Sun Hongcheng testified, I am the general manager and am solely responsible for distribution matters. I received a report from the factory director about the fire that night, but I was not at the scene at the time. Zhu Rutang testified that he was the chairman of the board. After receiving the report that night, he immediately inquired with the factory and was told that the fire started from Yongqing Lane due to a blowtorch. He did not know the rest of the details. Next, witness Zou Bukun from the plaintiff side testified that after the factory fire on the night of August 1st of last year, he was elected as a representative by 91 tenants and hired lawyer Wang to send a letter, requesting

repair of the brick wall. The former factory director Qian Menglin came forward to negotiate with me and agreed to repair it within April. Later, because I went to Zhenjiang, the factory did not actually implement the previous agreement, so I did not urge them. At this point in the interrogation, defense lawyers Xu Jie and others rose to declare that the factory's equipment was inspected by the Shanghai Municipal Council's Factory Inspection Department from time to time, and they deemed it satisfactory. Furthermore, this fire was thoroughly investigated by the Chinese and Western detectives of the Putuo Road Police Station at the time. If they had determined that the defendant was at fault, they would have already filed a public prosecution. This point should be clarified by requesting the court to review

the police station's report. Judge Liu stated that the responsibility for this case was not yet clear and that further investigation was necessary. He also stated that the plaintiffs were all poor civilians living in hardship, and it was especially pitiful that they had suffered this fire disaster. Therefore, he advised the defendants to provide several hundred yuan in court as a temporary relief measure, which was not an admission of liability. The defendant's lawyer agreed with this point, but stated that the factory was currently occupied by the plaintiffs, preventing it from operating. It would be best to order the plaintiffs to move out completely within two or three days so that work could resume. Furthermore, many plaintiffs were present in court, and there were concerns that after the court adjourned, they might

cause disturbances to the defendants. This point should be noted. Judge Liu ordered the case to be adjourned until 4:10 p.m. on the 27th of this month for further questioning. If it was deemed necessary to conduct an on-site inspection, the lawyers of both parties would be notified to appear in court. The four defendants were each released on bail with a guarantor who would appear whenever summoned. Before the bail bonds were obtained, the defense lawyers were allowed to be responsible for their release, with a deadline of 12 p.m. tomorrow to submit the bail bonds. The defendant Qian Menglin, also known as Qian Zhenghua, was ordered to be summoned to court for trial. To maintain order, all plaintiffs were ordered to leave first. The court adjourned at 6 p.m. Soon after, the defendants and their defense lawyers boarded several cars, escorted by Chinese and Western detectives from the police station, and left.

Li Guocheng Had Been Sentenced to Death; Sentence Changed to Life Imprisonment After Retrial; Li Still Dissatisfied and Decides to Appeal Again 121

On August 15th of the 20th year of the Republic of China, at around 6 p.m., in room number two of the Fa Shang Hotel, located at No. 112 Xinxiao Bridge Street in the French Concession, Jiangbei bandits shot and killed Jiang Zhonghan, also known as Chen Yiming, and Xia Yongsheng, and wounded Zhong Ziqing. The culprit escaped the scene. The next day, the French police arrested Yan Jinbiao, also known as Yan Er, also known as Yan Dongpo, from Funing, who confessed that he was instigated by Li Guocheng and colluded with Yang Jiucheng, Liu Wu, Zhang San, and others, who were at large, to shoot and kill. The police sent Yan to the Second Special Court for public prosecution, and Yan was sentenced to death. During the appeal period, Yan's family captured Li Guocheng in Rihui Port, South Shanghai, and sent him to the Public Security Bureau. They submitted a petition to the Second Special Court to have Li brought back and handed over to the police for investigation and public prosecution. During the trial, Yan was repeatedly brought in for confrontation. As a result, Li was also sentenced to death and deprived of civil rights for life. Subsequently, Yan went through three trials and the original verdict was upheld. In early April of the 22nd year, the Third High Court sent him to the Caohejing Prison for execution by hanging. Li also disagreed with the verdict and appealed to the Third High Court, but the appeal was rejected. He then appealed to the Supreme Court, which reviewed the entire case file and found that there were doubts as to whether Li Guocheng was actually present at the scene to participate in the killings. According to the victim Jiang Zhonghan, when he was in the hospital, the police brought the captured Yan Jinbiao for identification, and Jiang said that he only recognized Yan Er as the assailant and did not mention Li Guocheng being at the scene. Therefore, there were doubts about Li's criminal conduct. The Supreme Court ruled to overturn the original verdict and send it back to the Third High Court for retrial. The Third High Court has already conducted a retrial with witness testimony, and the details have been reported in the newspapers. The case has already been declared closed for debate. Yesterday was the date for the verdict. At 9 a.m., Criminal Division Chief Guo Dezhang, along with Judges Xiong Huiping and Wang Yue, specially opened the Third Criminal Court and ordered the appellant Li Guocheng to be brought to the case and announced the verdict. The original verdict was overturned, and Li Guocheng was sentenced to life imprisonment for premeditated murder and deprived of civil rights for life. The official also explained the meaning of the verdict to Li and informed him that if he disagreed with the verdict, he could submit a petition to the court within ten days after receiving the judgment and appeal to the Supreme Court. After the announcement, Li was ordered to be returned to the detention center to await instructions. It is reported that Li still expressed dissatisfaction with this retrial verdict and decided to appeal again.

After Completion of the Shanghai-Wuxi Highway, Traffic Opens on August 10th; Location is Luyang Bridge at the Border of the City and Province; Driving Schedule and Fares Have Been Determined 122

After the completion of the Shanghai-Wuxi Highway project, it was immediately taken over by the Shanghai-Wuxi Long-Distance Bus Company. A shareholders' meeting and board of directors meeting were scheduled, and the driving schedule and fares have been determined. The opening ceremony is scheduled for August 10th at Luyang Bridge, the border between Shanghai and Jiangsu Province. Details are as follows:

Joint Acceptance: The Shanghai-Wuxi line of the Shanghai-Wuxi Highway is 140 kilometers long, and the Changshu-Suzhou branch line is 40 kilometers long. Both are gravel roads. Construction started on April 20th of last year and has now been completed. The Shanghai-Wuxi Long-Distance Bus Company sent Assistant Manager Zhu Kaichou and others from Shanghai to Wuxi to inspect the route and returned to Shanghai on the 15th. They will immediately jointly accept the highway with the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Construction's Highway Department and hold a shareholders' meeting of the company on July 28th to submit a report and discuss various important cases.

Opening Ceremony: The opening ceremony of the Shanghai-Wuxi Highway will definitely not be held on August 1st. According to the New Voice News Agency, it is scheduled for August 10th at Luyang Bridge, the border between Shanghai and Jiangsu Province, between Zhenru and Nanxiang. However, it must be jointly decided by the Shanghai-Wuxi Long-Distance Bus Company, the Shanghai Municipal Government, and the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Construction through further discussions. The Shanghai-Wuxi Long-Distance Bus Company has been actively preparing for the opening ceremony in recent days.

Schedule and Fares: The Shanghai-Wuxi Long-Distance Bus Company has equipped 65 long-distance buses, each capable of accommodating 50 passengers. They are currently parked at the Shanghai-Tai Long-Distance Bus Company station in Zhabei. The buses are painted lake green on the top and blue on the bottom, with two white stripes in the middle, and are very well arranged. The entire route is divided into three sections: (1) Shanghai to Changshu, (2) Changshu to Wuxi, and (3) Changshu to Suzhou. Each line will run 12 round trips per day. The fare is set at three cents per kilometer. During the opening period, there will be a 20% discount, making it 2.4 cents per kilometer. The driving schedule and fares have been determined and will be announced after approval by the board of directors.

Firefighters from Jiangwan Town Accused of Burning Religious Statues; Trial Concluded Yesterday, Verdict to be Announced Later 124

On April 30th of this year, residents of Jiangwan Town organized a festival to welcome the gods, carrying the three idols of the Liu Shrine around the area. As a result, an incident occurred. That evening, one of the idols was carried to an open space and burned, causing a great uproar. Afterward, the residents accused the fire brigade of initiating this action. The local police station detained Xu Liangzuo (35 years old), the captain of the fire brigade, Ni Ganchen (13 years old), Cao Weirui (26 years old), an employee, and Yin Daoxiang (17 years old, all from Jiangwan), and sent them to the local court. Prosecutor Xie Lian investigated the case and filed a public prosecution for property damage, stating that the defendants were all employees of the Jiangwan Fire Brigade. During the traditional festival to welcome the gods, the defendants had a verbal conflict and, in a fit of anger, burned three public idols of the East Temple in the town, rendering them unholy. The Shanghai Municipal Government ordered the Public Security Bureau to send the defendants to court. The investigation revealed that the fire brigade, under the guise of maintaining order, burned three wooden puppets in the open after the crowd dispersed. The facts were clear, and Xu Liangzuo and the other three defendants were released on bail pending further instructions. Yesterday at 11 a.m., Criminal Division Chief Cai Dingcheng specially opened the Third Court for the trial. The defendants hired lawyers Yao Yunbo and Zhang Zhuochen to defend them. Ni Ganchen testified first, stating that he was sick at home that day and was not present at the scene of the incident. The judge asked if he ran away when he saw the incident, and he replied no. The judge ordered Xu Liangzuo to the stand and asked why he burned the statues. He replied that it was the residents who burned them. Cao Weirui testified that he was not present at the scene of the incident and could be investigated. He claimed that he was unjustly detained in the police station for eight days. The judge asked if it was not the fire brigade who burned them, who did? He replied that he did not know. Yin Daoxiang testified that he and others were ordered by Captain Xu Liangzuo to be on duty, but he did not know who burned the idols. At this point, Prosecutor Xie arrived in court to deliver his closing argument. Then, the defendants' lawyers rose to speak for a long time, stating that the current trend is to eliminate superstition and that the defendants did not actually burn the statues. At most, they were scapegoats and requested that they be declared innocent. The judge considered the trial concluded and set a date

for the verdict to be announced on the 10th.

Caohejing Prison Actively Improving; Handling of Statistics Has Received International Acclaim 128

The Caohejing Jiangsu Second Prison (i.e., the Model Prison) has a long history since its establishment. It is now planning to expand significantly, build new dormitories, and improve facilities. At the same time, it will also provide education to the prisoners, which is truly a blessing for the prisoners. The details are as follows:

Expanding the New Prison: The prison is directly under the Ministry of Justice. The original prison buildings were built before the early years of the Republic, and a large number of houses were added a few years ago. It was originally planned to accommodate 1,300 prisoners (the old buildings can accommodate 800 people, and the new buildings can accommodate 500 people). However, the number of prisoners sent from all parties has reached more than 3,000. There are 600 military prisoners, more than 100 political prisoners, 200 female prisoners, 500 prisoners held by the First Special Court of the Special Zone, 800 prisoners held by the Second Special Zone of the French Concession, 80 prisoners held by various counties, and other prisoners from various places. The prison is overcrowded. The prison plans to add a new prison, and has purchased more than 20 mu of land

to build ordinary prison cells, a hospital prison, and the surrounding walls have been built. The funds have also been allocated in the amount of tens of thousands of yuan. The construction can begin as soon as it is approved by the Ministry of Justice.

Improving Facilities: The prison is also making every effort to improve the internal facilities. The planned hospital prison will adopt the latest equipment and can accommodate 200 people. At the same time, educators will be set up to do their best to educate and reform the prisoners. In addition, prisoners will be given freehand exercises and breathing exercises every morning, all for the purpose of improving the prisoners' lives.

Handling Fingerprints: The prison has recently developed a fingerprint science, which is categorized in a very thorough manner. For all prisoners, as long as a fingerprint is examined, it can be found out whether they have committed crimes in the past, which is very helpful in investigation procedures. In addition, the prison is also handling statistics, including the prisoners' origin, occupation, age, etc., all of which are very detailed. This type of work is the most modern equipment in the world. Last year, an exhibition was held in the capital of Belgium, and the prison also participated with this type of statistics, which was well received.

North Station; Rickshaw Puller Returns Lost Money 129

The North Station of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways has implemented a system for rickshaw pullers to escort passengers, which has been reported in this newspaper many times. The implementation of this system has greatly benefited passengers, and passengers who forget their belongings can be traced at any time. It is reported that an elderly woman surnamed Guo, who lives at No. 56 Yongfeng Lane, North Sichuan Road, took the Nanjing Express train to Shanghai at 11:30 p.m. the day before yesterday. At that time, she purchased a ticket and took a rickshaw with license No. 2524 from the Concession to her residence. She forgot a handbag on the rickshaw, containing more than 22 yuan. The rickshaw puller Sun Sancai found it and handed it over to the Samsung Rickshaw Company, which forwarded it to the Railway Bureau for the owner to claim. According to the Railway Bureau, the rickshaw tickets sold have two coupons. When the passenger arrives at their destination, they tear off the first coupon and give it to the rickshaw puller. The second coupon must be kept in case of lost items, so that they can be traced. If passengers can strictly implement this procedure, it will not only greatly protect the safety of individuals and their belongings, but also add a layer of powerful protection.

The Hurricane That Swept Through Shanghai the Night Before Last: Houses Collapsed, People Were Injured, and Boats Capsized 130

Eleven Workers Injured at a Foreign Warehouse. At 7:30 PM the night before last, a hurricane swept through Shanghai. At the Xinyu Foreign Warehouse (formerly known as Xietai Warehouse), located at No. 3 Yangjiadu Ferry, Pudong, the tiled factory connecting to the gatehouse collapsed, covering an area of approximately twenty feet. Dozens of workers were inside, seeking shelter from the heat. Seeing the factory shake violently, they scrambled to escape, but eleven workers were unable to flee in time and were injured. Yang Zhongquan, the chief of the Yangjiabo police station, along with several patrol officers, sergeants, and police officers, arrived at the scene to investigate. Together with Wang Yingcai, the warehouse manager, they arranged for the injured to be taken to the Pudong Hospital for treatment. It has been determined that the following four individuals sustained relatively serious injuries: Wang Datianzi (from Suqian), Lu Xianting (from Suqian), Sun Jinxiang (from Suqian), and Chen Xuetian (from Hubei). The following four sustained less severe injuries: Lü Daxi, Zhu Decheng, Ming Changquan, and Zhai Yishuang (all from Suqian). The following three did not require hospitalization: Chi Yongxiang, Gu Dachun, and Ming De.

Chen Jianglin's Soda Ash Boat. Chen Jianglin, a resident of Pudong, makes a living as a boatman. He owns more than ten barges, transporting goods for various foreign firms. At around 3:00 PM the day before yesterday, he loaded two barges full of soda ash from a certain foreign firm. While sailing with the tide toward the Longhua Cape shoreline at around 7:20 PM, they were suddenly struck by a violent storm. The boatman lost control, and both boats capsized in the Huangpu River. All the soda ash fell into the river, resulting in considerable losses. It is reported that they were fully insured for marine risks. The boat crew was rescued by neighboring vessels, and fortunately, no one drowned.

Xu Zhaosheng's Soybean Boat. Xu Zhaosheng, a barge owner, has one barge that specializes in transporting soybeans and oil cakes for the Changde Oil Mill. The day before yesterday afternoon, he received more than 700 bags of soybeans from a foreign warehouse in Yangjiadu to be delivered to the mill. However, as he approached the Changde Oil Mill shoreline in the Nanshi area at around 7:50 PM, the wind and rain suddenly intensified. The helmsman was unable to moor the boat, and it capsized. All the soybean bags fell into the river, resulting in significant losses. The boat was not insured. The crew members were rescued, and workers are currently being hired to salvage the soybean bags.

Yang Jinggui's Brick and Tile Boat. Yang Jinggui's boat, loaded with bricks and tiles, was sailing from the Dujia Hang area of southern Shanghai on the Huangpu River towards Shanghai. During the storm, the bridge was blown apart, causing him to lose control of the vessel. Seeing this, Yang immediately instructed the helmsman to steer towards the riverbank to seek shelter. However, the rudder was buffeted by the wind and waves, making it difficult to steer. The boat crashed head-on into the shoreline, damaging the bow and causing it to take on water. It also struck and damaged the stern of a small Jiangbei boat moored nearby. Negotiations are underway with Yang. When the mast of Yang's boat was blown down, two helmsmen fell into the river.

Wei Asheng's Flour Boat. Wei Asheng, a boatman from Pudong, loaded 300 bags of flour and other goods in Shanghai. During the heavy storm the night before last, as he sailed to the southern end of the newly opened Henan River in southern Huangpu, Wei saw the wind and rain and was heading towards the shore to drop anchor and moor. However, the cargo was very heavy, and the boat was buffeted by the wind and waves and capsized near the shore. A small steamer and other boats helped rescue Wei and his four crew members. The next morning, Wei managed to salvage the boat. A considerable amount of cargo was lost, and the goods on board were soaked in water, resulting in significant losses.

A Woman Carries Red Pills in Her Trousers: Miss Wang Arrested 132

Miss Wang, a 50-year-old woman from Yangzhou, has recently been transporting red pills for those engaged in the profitable drug trade. She mainly carries them from the French Concession for sale on Yangshupu Road. This was discovered by Song Bingzheng, a Chinese detective from the Narcotics Division of the Public Concession Police. At around 6:00 AM the day before yesterday, he and several detectives waited for a while near Ningguo Road on Yangshupu Road. Miss Wang arrived, and they stepped forward and ordered her to stop. They knew that the drugs were hidden in her trousers. Because there was no female investigator present, they could not search her and planned to take her to the police station. As Miss Wang passed an open space, she suddenly claimed that she needed to urinate. Taking advantage of the opportunity, she threw a bag of red pills weighing six ounces into a sewer in an attempt to get away with it. However, the detectives saw her, immediately retrieved the bag, and she claimed that a child downstairs at the Yuebin Hotel in the French Concession had given her the red pills. They went to the hotel to investigate, but this was not the case. She then claimed that Hua Xiangping, a resident of No. 51 Maoxian Lane, had asked her to deliver the pills to Erbao in Puai Lane on Yangshupu Road for sale. They went to No. 51 to arrest Hua, but he had already fled. Miss Wang and the evidence were taken to the Yangshupu Police Station and transferred to the women's detention center. Yesterday morning, she was taken to the Third Criminal Division of the First Special District Court. Wang Yaotang, a lawyer from the Public Works Department, detailed the events. Subsequently, the Chinese and foreign detectives reported the process of arresting the defendant and presented the evidence for inspection. Questioned about it, the defendant confessed to carrying the red pills for Hua and receiving ten cents for each packet. She gave evasive answers to other questions. Judge Wu Zehan ordered her to be remanded in custody and scheduled a court hearing.

He Dared to Commit Assault While Using Counterfeit Coins 133

Hong Chenglin, a vegetable vendor from Anhui, went to the Hongkou vegetable market on Hanzhong Road at around 5:00 AM the day before yesterday. He tried to buy vegetables from Yan Jinrong, a vendor from Dachang, with two counterfeit twenty-cent coins. Yan discovered the fraud and refused to exchange them, and Hong beat Yan, causing him to fall to the ground and call for help. Detective Ding Baoxiang and Officer No. 1883 arrived after hearing the commotion. After understanding the situation, they arrested Hong and found nine similar counterfeit twenty-cent coins on his person. He was taken to the Hongkou Police Station and detained. Yesterday morning, he was taken to the Eleventh Criminal Division of the Special Court. Wang Yaotang, a lawyer from the Public Works Department, described the events and requested an adjournment to investigate the source of the counterfeit coins. Subsequently, the victim and the arresting officers reported the events. The counterfeit coins were presented for inspection. When questioned, the defendant gave evasive answers. Judge Wu Zehan ordered him to be remanded in custody and scheduled another date for investigation and judgment.

Suicide Due to Inability to Repay Debt: The Loss of Shen Jinlin, Who Lent Most of the Money to His Friend Shen Jinlin, Is So Pitiable. 134

Shen Jinlin, a 38-year-old local employee of the Anglo-American Tobacco Company's accounting department, lived at No. 61, Lane 49, Zhangjia House, Avenue Edward VII. Recently, due to his inability to repay a debt of several thousand dollars to the company, he became despondent on the morning of the tenth of this month and took his own life by secretly ingesting opium. When his family discovered him, they sent him to Baolong Hospital, but the treatment was ineffective. He died from the effects of the poison the day before yesterday. The hospital reported the incident to the Xinzha Police Station, which ordered Detective Yang Youshan to investigate. The body was then taken to the Faillon Road morgue. Yesterday morning, Guo Wei, a prosecutor from the First Special District Court, along with forensic doctor Zhang Yan, clerk Wang Zuyi, and others, arrived at the morgue to examine the body. Shen Zongwang, 18, a student, testified that the deceased was his father. He had embezzled $8,000 from the company, of which $5,000 had been borrowed by his friend. He did not have a loan document, so he was unable to recover the money. This made his father feel even more sad and angry, and he unexpectedly took this step, etc. After receiving the testimony, Guo concluded that the deceased, Shen Jinlin, male, had died from ingesting opium. The body was handed over to his son, Shen Zongwang, who signed a statement and took the coffin back.

Stable Boy Beats Foreman to Death 135

Wang Shunlai, a 39-year-old from Ningbo, was the deputy foreman under Wu Fuchun, the foreman at the Jiangwan Race Club's stable. At 7:20 PM on the 22nd of last month, Wang Shunlai and Ma Xiaoer (from Tianjin), a stable boy, had an argument over work matters. At first, they ridiculed each other, but Ma, who was hot-tempered, became furious and resorted to violence, punching Wang. Wang was caught off guard and fell to the ground. Wang, not to be outdone, jumped up and fought back. They wrestled into a ball, and their companions tried their best to separate them. Because Ma Xiaoer was as strong as an ox and had someone else (at large) helping him, Wang Shunlai was no match for him and suffered internal injuries. After returning home, Wang felt a pain in his lower back and sought treatment from an injury specialist, but it was ineffective. He died at home at 5:45 PM the day before yesterday. His wife, Wang Dongshi, reported to the Jiangwan Police Station that her husband had been beaten to death by Ma Xiaoer. The police immediately arrested Ma Xiaoer and detained him. Yesterday morning, the deceased's brother-in-law, He Axing, submitted a petition to the procuratorate of the District Court, requesting an autopsy to clear the deceased's name. After receiving the petition, the court commissioned Prosecutor Lei Binzhang and Examiner Xuan Zhiming to conduct an autopsy in the afternoon.

After getting off the train, they will board a dedicated boat to visit the local attractions near Wujiang. That evening, they will take the 9:00 PM Shanghai-Wuxi special train back to Shanghai. The cost is three yuan per person, including boat transportation and meals. Registration has already begun at the association's special district branch on the third floor of the Continental Department Store on Nanjing Road. Doctor Jin Songpan's New Method of Smoking Cessation 145

Jing'an Hospital, Jing'an Villa, Jing'an Temple Road, has recently invented a method of smoking cessation that is completely different from ordinary methods. According to Doctor Jin Songpan, who gave a detailed explanation yesterday, he said that he used to work in the military and saw the harm caused by smoking. Red pills and white powder were particularly harmful. Therefore, he vowed to complete a method of quitting smoking. At first, he used blood drawing, blistering, and other methods. Later, according to the principles of pharmacology, all highly poisonous drugs can be neutralized, so he studied and tested them, and finally got this method. After that, quitting smoking is not difficult. It's like 606 treating syphilis, quinine treating malaria, and blood serum treating various diseases. Using this new medicine, injection on time will eliminate the tobacco poison throughout the body. Only then will the excrement of various organs have an unusual odor. After the tobacco poison is eliminated, you will never want to smoke again, and all diseases will be eliminated. The spirit feels unusually comfortable. Now he is very willing to make this method widely promoted, but his personal ability is limited. If the support of powerful people can be obtained, or the government can sponsor it, the amount will be large and the effect will be rapid. However, no matter what, we will now do our best to promote it. Dr. Jin has served as the chief of the military medical department of the Whampoa Military Academy, the chief of the military medical department of the general headquarters, the chief of the field hygiene department of the general headquarters of the first and second Northern Expeditions, and the director of the statistics department of the Ministry of Health. His knowledge and experience are excellent. Now he is in Shanghai.

Italian Open-Air School 153

Integrating Compulsory Education and Health Education as a Pioneer in Eliminating Illiteracy in Italy

—Simple Equipment Worthy of Reference for Our Literacy Movement—

(Special dispatch from Rome) Our country has recently recognized that illiteracy is an obstacle to national rejuvenation and is sparing no effort in promoting literacy movements. The Italian open-air school, "Scuola Aperta," has simple equipment but achieves significant results, which is worthy of good reference for our country's efforts in promoting civic education today. Xue Guangqian, the president of the Shanghai Society, who studied in Rome, Italy, has provided the following dispatch on its organization and activities, which can be used as a practical reference for our country.

Objectives

The objectives of establishing Italian open-air schools are to promote compulsory education and health education. Children from impoverished families and those with weak health can enter free of charge to receive appropriate education. These schools are entirely established by the state and are widespread in various locations. The one established in Rome, Italy, has the longest history and the largest scope. The country recognizes that the life of the nation is tied to children. Children in superior circumstances naturally have suitable families to raise them, which can be disregarded. However, children who are impoverished and weak must be the responsibility of the state to provide guidance and protection.

Admission Requirements

Any child from the age of six to fourteen who is unable to attend ordinary schools or who is physically weak and often in an unhealthy state, after passing a doctor's examination and being deemed suitable for this type of school life, can enter free of charge. The school provides transportation to and from school every day. This transportation responsibility is handled by the street leader of each street (according to the Italian Fascist Party, each street has a street leader whose sole duty is to serve the public), so parents do not need to worry about it. Lunch and dinner are also provided by the school free of charge. Although it is only one soup and one dish, the cost is minimal, but it is nutritious and very hygienic. We know that the slogan for Italian children is "books" and "guns." Only those who are knowledgeable and physically strong are considered ideal and healthy citizens.

School Facilities

The school facilities are very simple, mostly located in large open-air gardens, with a few wooden houses inside, which are also very rudimentary, probably the reason why it is called an open-air school. The children's clothing consists of a shirt and trousers for girls, nothing else. Boys only wear trousers and are naked on the upper body (in winter, they wear a woolen shirt). Daily reading and operation allow them to live under the sunlight, which can enhance children's interest in nature and benefit their physical and mental strength. In addition to the necessary teachers, the school also has several doctors who pay close attention to the nutrition and health of the children at all times and conduct strict examinations.

Activities

The school's activities primarily focus on children's direct operation. Teachers are entirely in a guiding and cooperative role. All the children in the school are divided into groups of six to be responsible for washing, sweeping, cleaning, and cooking lunch. For example, for lunch, four people share a small table. All arrangements, food utensils, distributing food and vegetables, and washing dishes are all handled by the children themselves. In addition, the school is planted with various flowers, fruits, and vegetables, which are also irrigated and planted by the children. Since these children come from poor families, everything they learn can help their parents in their work. The teaching time is based on the principle of not using textbooks. Teachers explain orally, and older children must take notes. All reading materials, paper, and pens are provided by the school.

Source of Funds

The key to Italy's revitalization lies in economizing and rationalizing everything, using the minimum cost to obtain the maximum benefit, and seeking the most significant results in the shortest period. The open-air school is one of them. Although the open-air school is a large undertaking, the economic cost to the state is very limited. Its location is an open-air space, borrowed from the public and free of charge (or contacted with private parks, requesting them to open for borrowing). All the wood for the simple school buildings and school equipment, and all the objects used in teaching materials, are generally solicited by the school from all parties. Collecting bits to make a fur robe and accumulating small amounts into large sums. All parties also know that open-air schools are set up to help poor and weak children, so everyone is willing to do their best to fulfill the spirit and obligation of human mutual assistance. Before Mussolini came to power in Italy, illiteracy was widespread, roughly equivalent to China today (according to statistics, the percentage of illiterate people in Sardinia in southern Italy was 70% or more). Now that knowledge has developed and education has become widespread, the open-air school is the most powerful pioneering tool in this process. Today, China deeply feels that the urgency of eliminating illiteracy cannot be delayed. It is worthwhile to adopt and refer to the open-air school in Italy, which has achieved great results. However, due to the difficulties of China's finances, and the need for construction is even more complicated, so today, how to make things economical and rational, to use one person to do two people's work, and one penny to work as two penny, is the prerequisite for everything. The literacy movement is just one example.

Dr. Wu Youxun Elected as a Member of the German Academy of Natural Sciences 154

Dr. Wu Youxun, head of the Department of Physics at National Tsinghua University in Beiping, was recently elected as a member of the German Academy of Natural Sciences (Deutsche Akademie der Naturforscher) in Halle, Germany. Professor Emil Abderhalden, the president of the academy, has sent a letter to Wu, which is translated as follows: "Professor Wu Youxun, I am very pleased to inform you that at a recent regular meeting, our academy unanimously elected you as a member. This is to express our recognition and admiration for your special contributions to physics. I will send you a membership certificate. Very respectfully, Emil Abderhalden." The German Academy of Natural Sciences was founded in 1652 AD and is located in Halle, Germany. Its members are all world-renowned natural science experts who must have special contributions to their studies to be eligible for selection. Wu's selection this time is the first for the Chinese scientific community. This is not only an honor for Wu personally but also the glory of the academic circles in our country. It is heard that Wu is from Jiangxi Province, graduated from Nanjing Higher Normal School, and has a Ph.D. in Physics from the University of Chicago in the United States. He was a research faculty member at the University of Chicago and the head of the Department of Physics at Nanjing National Central University. Since 1928, he has been a professor of physics at National Tsinghua University. In addition to his position at Tsinghua, he is also employed as a contract researcher at the National Central Research Institute and a special researcher at the National Beiping Research Institute.
