The Chinese Mathematical Society Will Be Established 159

The inaugural meeting will be held on the 25th of this month. The venue is borrowed from Jiaotong University in Xujiahui.

In recent years, there have been many academic groups in China, such as physics, chemistry, biology, geography, astronomy, and geology societies. However, there is still a lack of organizations purely for the study of mathematics. Domestic mathematics circles, including Xiong Dizhi, Gu Yangwu, Hu Dunfu, Zhou Meiquan, Feng Hanshu, He Lu, Sun Guangyuan, Zhu Gongjin, Su Buqing, Zeng Zhaoan, Fan Huiguo, Huang Jiyu, Jiang Zehan, and He Yanxuan, have initiated the organization of the Chinese Mathematical Society. After several months of discussion, universities in China have expressed their support. Preparations are now complete, and the inaugural meeting will be held at the National Jiaotong University in Xujiahui, Shanghai, on the 25th, 26th, and 27th of this month. It is expected to add a unique luster to the academic community in our country.

Zhang Shilu Returns to China After Lecturing in Japan 160

Zhang Shilu, a professor at Jinan University, was invited by the Chinese Language Society run by the Japanese to lecture on Chinese linguistics in Tokyo. He stayed there for about two weeks and gave three lectures. The first lecture was at the East Asia Tongwen Society, the venue for the Chinese Language Society's general meeting, on the topic of "The Phonological System of the Chinese Language." From the evolutionary history of Chinese phonetics, he inferred the long history of Chinese national culture, which was enough to move the hearts of the Japanese. The second lecture was at the East Asia Higher Preparatory School, an open lecture for students from various schools, on the topic of "The Characteristics of the Chinese Language and the Evolution of Language." The third lecture was at the invitation of Professor Takeda Fuku and others from the Imperial University, attending the Siwen Society, lecturing on "The Problem of the Subdivisions in Guangyun." This topic was more specialized. Professors and older people with beards from various schools came to listen to each lecture, taking notes non-stop, even for three or four hours without fatigue. After the lecture, they would often ask questions and inquire earnestly. The Japanese spirit of valuing academics is truly admirable. As for Zhang's feelings about this trip, he deeply feels that if we want to talk about saving the country, we must first save ourselves. We do not necessarily have to join the army or engage in politics to save the country. We can improve and deepen our studies within the scope of our respective responsibilities or what we should and want to learn, to show our achievements, which is enough to enhance the status of the country and prevent being looked down upon by anyone. This is the only true way to save the country.

Chiang Kai-shek Commends Yan Deji 162

Subsidizing the Huanghuagang Middle School's construction costs of 100,000 yuan

Yan Deji, a revolutionary giant in Sichuan, was recently summoned by Chairman Chiang to the province to meet and receive instructions. He has met with Chairman Chiang, who inquired about the recent situation in detail. Yan reported on his past participation in revolutionary work, and Chiang commended him and asked him to wait for the central government to assign him to an important position. Since Yan returned from Japan during the late Qing Dynasty and participated in the revolutionary work, on March 29th, one year before the Republic of China, the Guangzhou Uprising, Yan participated in important work. The matter was revealed and the collection failed. Fortunately, Yan managed to escape. In 1932, Yan raised funds in Shanghai to establish Huanghuagang Middle School to commemorate the martyrs and promote the national spirit, achieving remarkable results. Recently, the Central Party Department has approved the establishment of the school, which Chiang praised greatly. It is heard that a subsidy of 100,000 yuan will be granted to build school buildings to expand the school.

Zhijiang High School Restores Business Courses 163

After Zhijiang High School resumed operation in 1929, it originally had three departments: business, architecture, and general studies. In 1931, for some reason, it only operated the general studies department. Recently, in view of the social need for business talents and in order to promote vocational education, it has been approved by the Education Department to restore business courses starting in 1935 and enroll first-year freshmen. The principal of the school was originally concurrently held by Huang Shijin, the director of the Department of Education at the university. Recently, as the university department will add a counseling department from the next year, and Huang will be in charge, the position of principal of the high school has been replaced by Zhang Wenchang, the director of academic affairs. Zhang will still hold the position of director of academic affairs concurrently. The school, in view of the fact that many promising students from poor families cannot afford to attend, has specially proposed 1,000 yuan from the budget from the next academic year as a subsidy for poor students. Whether new or old students, those who are in the top rank in both academic and conduct and whose families are poor can apply. There are a total of ten places this time. Each student can receive 50 yuan free of charge per semester. Therefore, students who receive this subsidy only need to pay more than 50 yuan for the first semester for food and uniforms, and old students only need to pay more than 40 yuan per semester. The school's science, library, dormitory, sports, and medical facilities are already well-equipped. Starting next academic year, it is heard that a middle school equipment committee will be specially established to improve middle school equipment. Physics and biology instruments, wall charts, models, and history and geography wall charts will all be added.

Spring and Autumn

Snippets 176

— (Chan Chen)

Life is like a battlefield. If we stop wielding our spears and swords, we will immediately be attacked by the enemy. Ah! If we want to survive, we must fight with our entire lives!

The reason why human existence can be maintained, and the reason why life can obtain meaning and value, all depend on the result of striving for an ideal. Therefore, if a person has no ideal and cannot strive, then he will only forever fall into the predicament of lamenting that life is boring and uninteresting.

All great figures in ancient and modern times, both in China and abroad, all people with morality and meaningful lives, have forgotten the small self of their individual bodies and devoted themselves to the infinite greater self. Therefore, we can only obtain true meaning and value in life through this effort.

The Scenery of Lihong Bridge 177

— Zhang Muliang

The sky is just dawning, not yet fully bright, and everything is strangely silent. However, the manure wharf of Lihong Bridge is already crowded with men and women, moving out one manure cart after another lying on the manure wharf. A long line of manure carts makes a creaking sound on the asphalt road.

The sun slowly peeks out its red face from the clouds. Then, Lihong Bridge gradually becomes lively. The trolleybuses of routes seventeen and eighteen begin to run their routes, packed with batches of people going to work and people rushing to the early market.

In a flash, male and female students with schoolbags and people carrying菜 baskets to buy vegetables pass through Lihong Bridge in an endless stream, each with a different posture.

Especially a group of foreign vagrants (Russians) and beggars are particularly active. The foreign vagrants have learned a pure Mandarin accent and beg for money from close-by Chinese people, hoping to exchange it for a day of food and drink. The beggars' method of begging is that they wait for friends sitting in rickshaws to pass over the bridge, and then help the rickshaw pull over the bridge, and then beg for money from the friends sitting in the rickshaw. This situation is no different from the Old Gate Bridge and Tianhou Palace Bridge.

A red Ford card, strangely tall, with a machine gun mounted on it, is seated with nine patrolmen, how majestic! A gray Ford card followed behind, speeding quickly to Lihong Bridge. The beggars and foreign vagrants all shouted: "Hey: The red man's car is coming, run away quickly!"

Following the panicked shouts, the order on the road was in complete chaos. The imposing patrolmen had already caught several people like an eagle catching chicks, and the people who were watching the show all gathered together at the same time.

The police car, full of beggars and foreign vagrants, left with its bell ringing. Then, the air in Lihong Bridge temporarily felt a little calmer.

The weather gradually turned dark, and the manure wharf of Lihong Bridge was finally so silent, with two or three hundred manure carts lying there lifelessly, as if forming a manure cart kingdom.

The Life of a Dog 178

— Ji Yijie

I occasionally recall the two common sayings, "Better to be a dog in times of peace than a person in times of chaos," and think of several kinds of dog lives.

One type is the pampered Pekingese dog. There are very few of these dogs, probably not even one in a thousand. Its owner is either a foreigner or a modern woman. It is accustomed to a comfortable life, eating its fill all day long, doing nothing. Its food includes beef, toast, and eggs. It sleeps in a Western-style house and has a wire bed or a beautiful wool carpet. Sometimes it even gets to ride in a car. Its material enjoyment is truly worlds apart compared to all ordinary dogs.

One type is the tolerably well-fed kitchen dog, also known as a grass dog. There are not many of these dogs either, but about ten percent. It depends on the chef for a living. Although it cannot eat beef and eggs, it can eat its fill of white rice, leftover food, and cold dishes. Although it cannot sleep on a wool blanket or ride in a car, it is warm enough to take from a soft woodpile. Compared to other dogs, it is much more comfortable.

One type is the labor-style guard dog, mostly grass species. There are more of these dogs, accounting for about fifteen to twenty percent. However, the treatment it receives is very harsh. Its food is coarse grains, at most vegetable soup and meat bones. It sleeps on bluestone slabs or cement, which is lower than the kitchen dog.

One type is the unemployed stray dog. It has no owner. There are the most of these dogs now, almost everywhere you look. It runs in the streets all day long, exposed to rain and sun, unable to get its fill. It is forced to search for filth in garbage dumps or toilets to fill its stomach, making it the most unfortunate and pitiful of all dogs.

In summary, in today's world of economic depression, not to mention people, even dogs are affected.

Little Western Paradise 179

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Sixteen: The Screen Conceals Tears, It Is Difficult to Escape Cold Eyes; Fine Garments Flaunt Luck, Having Once Been to the Powerful Man's House

When he arrived in his room, the room attendant brought in tea and said with a smile: "Mr. Cheng, let me tell you a piece of news, that Zhu family girl has already been sold." Zhichan said: "Didn't you tell me last night?" The room attendant said with a smile: "I did say it last night, but if that girl had run away in the middle of the night, the deal wouldn't have been considered done. Now that the person has spent a night in Mr. Jia's arms, and the silver dollars have also spent a night in Mrs. Hu's pit, it is considered sold whether it is sold or not, and it is considered done whether it is done or not." Zhichan was washing his face, so he said lightly with a smile: "You all wish that such things would happen every day. No matter what, you can always get a few dimes as a happy money." The room attendant said with a smile: "We wouldn't want a few dimes for marrying such a virgin bride." Zhichan said: "Then, how much did Mr. Jia give you?" The room attendant said: "Not every room attendant gets something. You always have to be the person in charge to get a little benefit. I'm considered very good, I got three silver dollars." As he spoke, he revealed most of his teeth and laughed. Zhichan said: "You people who are dividing the spoils on the sidelines are laughing appropriately, but do you know that the person who sold herself is already crying very sadly." The room attendant was stunned and stood there and asked: "Mr. Cheng, did you see the bride crying?" Zhichan said: "No, no, I was just guessing like that." The room attendant didn't take his words to heart. He was busy in the morning and went to take care of the other rooms for the travelers. After a while, the room attendant hurriedly walked into the room and said to him in a low voice: "Mr. Cheng, you really guessed it, isn't that girl crying? Now that she has food to eat and clothes to wear, and her family for two generations won't starve to death, she should be happy. I don't understand why she has to cry." (266)

The Fragrant Mists of Imperial Incense 180

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

No matter what the thing was, she always felt that it was extremely irritating, so that she could no longer bear it, and said loudly:

"If we continue to sit here like this, it will really bore people to death. We must go out of the palace and stroll around in the long corridor." (Translator's Note: The long corridor is under the Paiyun Hall in the Summer Palace. Not only is it very long, but also it is constructed in an extremely magnificent way. People in the palace call it the long corridor). "Hurry up and prepare to go with me! Go and inform the others!"

Because when I was first summoned into the palace this morning, the Empress Dowager had already instructed me to stroke her forehead with my hand to test her temperature. Now that she wanted to go out, I automatically said that she should let me test her temperature. She immediately agreed; but I felt very embarrassed after trying it. Originally, although her fever had been reduced a lot compared to the morning, it had not yet returned to normal. When my palm covered her forehead, I still felt a little hot; looking at her spirit, it was still not very cheerful. I was originally a very enthusiastic person and very concerned about her, so I had no choice but to offer some advice.

"Old Buddha, please be patient for a while longer, okay?" I said: "Your fever has not completely subsided yet! It's best not to be exposed to the wind; walking in the long corridor is certainly more open than sitting in the palace, but it is inevitable that you will be exposed to the wind, and it is too hard!"

She was obviously shocked by these words: I was completely confused at the time. (366)

White-Haired Girl 181

— Qing Qu

"White-haired girl," this term has never been heard of before. In fact, it is not surprising, because although she is old, she is still like a maiden. She has never been engaged to anyone since she was a child. Therefore, her temples gradually turned white, and she unknowingly became the oldest owner in the family. Almost all the seven daily necessities are not handled by her. His surname and residence are temporarily hidden for him, but his life and experience are worth mentioning.

"White-haired girl," in terms of the same clan, the younger generation generally call him "Uncle ×," maidservants or even call him "Miss Tai," although his status has not been married, residing in a position of seniority, all accounting of silver and money, daily expenses, if not according to his budget, no matter which young master and young mistress, are not allowed to act without authorization, so "white-haired girl," since the death of his parents, in these thirty years, the fields and houses inherited have been kept without any shortage. Not only is the expenditure enough to spend, but also waiting for the younger brother who has been adopted to come of age, marry a wife, and maintain the bloodline of a surname, is this not a very respectable thing? Among the neighbors, hearing the reputation of "white-haired girl," some see him being able to take power, praising him as a "woman in man's clothing," some see him being good at managing the family, respecting him as a "heroine" who has restored the × surname, all啧啧称羡. You, if you don't mention "white-haired girl" then never mind, but if you ask about "white-haired girl," huh! You can dare say that everyone in this place knows it.

This year, a certain newspaper reported that it was "the year of old men getting married." One day, the "white-haired girl" saw it, and he laughed: "Alas! This is probably because the reporters made a mistake in the title. What is the reason? Isn't it that those who marry old men are all 'old maids'?" However, those "old maids," at first each held the principle of not marrying for life, but when they reached the age of fifty, I don't know why, they wanted to be a shy "new bride" once, I always feel a little unclear," these few words, "white-haired girl," said very humorously, so I made this small biography for him, to see that "white-haired girl" is indeed worthy of his name!

Social Realism

Dead End 182

— Zhu Yun

When I saw the news of Wen Xiaoxia's suicide in the newspaper, my heart skipped a beat. Xiaoxia was a young friend of mine and a neighbor; his round face and shy demeanor were endearing. But this young man actually committed suicide in a hotel, and as I looked at the photo of him in the newspaper, my heart was filled with endless sorrow.

Although Xiaoxia came from a humble family, he was so clever and eager to learn. Before I moved, Xiaoxia and I often played together. After I moved, driven by the pressures of life, I gradually became estranged from Xiaoxia. However, through his letters, I learned that he was an apprentice in a silk and satin shop. In five years, because of his prudence and intelligence, he had been promoted from apprentice to assistant to the chief accountant. That such a promising young man would commit suicide filled me with doubt.

According to the newspaper, Xiaoxia's suicide was due to unemployment and homelessness. How could such a cautious young man, whose shop had not closed down, become unemployed and homeless? To verify the cause of my friend's death, I prepared to make an on-site visit to the hotel where he committed suicide, but before I could leave, the postman in green delivered Xiaoxia's last letter of farewell to my hand.

With trembling hands, I tore open the envelope containing Xiaoxia's hurried handwriting. Inside were two sheets of stationery from the hotel, the handwriting so careless. The letter began with the sentence: "Dear Brother Yun, Xiaoxia has committed suicide!" It continued: "By the time this letter reaches your hands, the news of my suicide will have already met your eyes. The reason for my suicide, you may not believe. But I have indeed been dismissed from the shop and driven out of my home because of my excessive absurdity. This all started last summer when I met Lan Ying, the executioner who killed me, in the movie theater. She is a regular customer who often buys fabric from our shop, and we knew each other. We sat together, and she was so incredibly beautiful that we moved from talking about the movie to talking about everything. She was too captivating. One movie, and we became friends. Brother Yun, I have always considered myself a passionate man, and Lan Ying was truly enchanting. At the time, I felt it was such an honor that such a beauty would become my lover, so I often went out with her. Of course, I didn't pay attention to my duties at the shop, and to cover my expenses, I gradually embezzled from the funds I handled. As a result, in half a year, I embezzled over two hundred yuan. Fortunately, my master was kind and only dismissed me, without strictly pursuing the embezzled funds. When I returned home, my parents were, of course, furious, but I was so in love with Lan Ying that I felt carefree without a job. However, since I had no income and Lan Ying needed money, I disregarded everything and repeatedly stole and sold valuable items from home, until my father gave me a severe beating and drove me out. And Lan Ying, upon hearing the news of my expulsion, broke up with me. Brother Yun, I wanted to join the army, but my body has been so ruined that I am weak and useless. What can I do? It's over! Everything is over. Love is truly a dead end that lures one to suicide! Xiaoxia, last words."

After reading this letter, my hands trembled so much that I could not hold the tear-stained stationery. I listened as the wet letter fell to the ground, and I no longer had the strength to pick it up.

Grain: Speculation on Future Contracts Drives Rush to Cover Positions 188

Yesterday, the flour market showed firmness and stability due to surging prices of foreign wheat. Chicago rose by a significant 78 jiao, and Canada increased by 4 fen. Market sentiment was influenced by the rebound in foreign wheat prices and the continued severe flooding along the Yangtze and Yellow Rivers. As a result, some speculators rushed to cover their short positions. There was also some trading activity from customers, leading to consistently high asking prices across all contract months. However, manufacturers offered few supplies and remained cautious due to the lack of activity in spot foreign wheat. While current standards trended downwards, flour mills maintained a premium of 5 fen on existing flour stocks. This situation has persisted for the past three to four weeks with little change, representing a unique circumstance. Looking ahead, the key to price fluctuations lies entirely abroad, beyond the control of domestic conditions. Consequently, the current month's contract rose by 1 jiao 7 fen 5 li, August's by 2 fen 5 li, September and October's by 2 fen 2 xia-ban, November's by 2 fen, and December's by 1 fen 7 li 5 hao.

Ample Spot Wheat Leads to Decline in Wheat Futures 189

Yesterday morning, the wheat futures market initially showed gains across all contract months but then declined. The current month's contract opened lower by 5 fen due to the heavy accumulation of spot wheat and consistently sluggish demand from mills. There were no subsequent trades. Distant months initially gained 1-2 fen, buoyed by the rising prices of foreign wheat, but later fell back by 2-3 fen due to the weakness in the current month's contract. In the afternoon session, there were no trades in the current month's contract, and distant contracts remained quiet and lifeless due to the abundance of spot wheat. Looking ahead, a sustained stabilization is only expected when foreign wheat activity ceases. Consequently, August and September contracts each fell by 1 fen, and the October contract fell by 2 fen. The spot wheat market, which had been inactive for several days, finally opened yesterday with prices for various grades of ship and railcar wheat falling by a substantial 1 jiao. Kaiwu wheat was priced at 3 yuan 3 jiao 2 fen, Liuhe wheat at 3 yuan 3 jiao 3-4 fen, Wuyi wheat at 3 yuan 2 jiao 9 fen, Jiangjiazhen Yangzhou wheat at 3 yuan 2 jiao 8 fen, Yaowan wheat at 3 yuan 3 jiao 3 fen, Puzhen wheat at 3 yuan 2 jiao 2 fen (and even down to 2 jiao), Nanjing and Hezhou wheat at 3 yuan 1 jiao 8 fen, Zhengyi wheat at 3 yuan 2 jiao 8-9 fen, and Yanghe wheat at 3 yuan 3 jiao 5 hao. Fuxin took 9,000 bags, and Xinda took 500 bags.

Rice Prices Continue to Fall 190

Yesterday, the supply of rice (South Shanghai) remained scarce, with only 7-8 boats arriving (totaling 15-16 hundred loads). While sales in the local market were sluggish, orders continued to come in from Tianjin, Weihaiwei, and other regions for 6-7 hundred bags of various premium japonica and thin indica rices, which were mostly settled. Only medium-grade rice continued to fall by over 1 jiao. There were reports of a significant turnaround in Zhabei yesterday afternoon, raising hopes for a similar improvement in the South Shanghai market today. Refined rice continued to depreciate, with no market for lower-grade rice. (21-22 boats from North Shanghai). The sales of various grades of rice were as follows: white japonica slightly improved, early rice with fixed prices saw some transactions, thin indica was flat with limited sales, and white rice slightly improved. The market price for white japonica fell another 1-2 jiao, thin indica fell by about 2 jiao, early rice fell by 3-4 jiao, and white rice fell by 2-3 jiao. Other grades of rice also showed weakness.

Sales of imported rice remained active, with more significant volumes going to regions along the Yangtze River, such as Jiujiang, Hankou, Shashi, as well as the Beiyang hinterland. However, transaction volumes were limited, failing to shift the market price trend. Furthermore, goods already fixed at favorable prices were still being loaded and shipped, and imported rice destined for Ningbo was also being diverted to Shanghai. With the hot weather, river wharves were under pressure to expedite deliveries, and trading houses were also lowering prices to stimulate sales, resulting in relatively active sales but a continued slight decline of about 1 jiao in market prices. The total volume released to the market was 7,000 bags of Saigon rice, 1,700 bags of Little Unity rice, and 600 bags of Siamese rice, distributed among various trading houses.

Wenzhou New Soybeans Arrive in Shanghai 191

Excellent Quality, Poor Prices; Soybean Cake Weakens Further, Soybean Oil Rises Again

However, it is said that the cost price of these soybeans is 4 yuan 1-2 jiao, so future arrivals are not expected to be numerous. Old soybeans remained difficult to sell in a sluggish market with weak prices. Soybean cake initially tightened but then weakened, while soybean oil was viewed favorably with strong demand, leading to market tightness and another increase of 2 jiao in price compared to the previous day.

Silk and Tea: Foreign Firms' Tea Market Slightly Quiet 192

Since the beginning of last month, green teas from Lu, Tu, and other regions have seen strong sales to European firms for both retail and wholesale due to their low prices. The market has remained stable for over a month, and prices have gradually rebounded by over 10 yuan after a significant drop at the opening of the season. However, in the past two days, a certain British firm, considering Chinese tea merchants' asking prices to be excessive, has become more cautious in its purchases of various grades of premium eyebrow green tea. Given its substantial sales volume, the market has become quieter as a result. However, current green tea inventories in the market are low, and the supply of raw tea from all regions is exhausted. The total green tea production volume is 30% lower than last year, so the market should remain stable.

The supply of domestically produced refined cotton and red sugar increased slightly, leading to a weakening trend. Free Talk

Bedbug Night Talk 197

— Tang Tao

In my article "Seeing and Thinking," I mentioned that the superficial and confused thinking prevalent today is a mixture of Confucianism, Taoism, and Zen Buddhism, but I did not explain how this mixture came about. On a hot summer night, tormented by bedbugs, unable to sleep no matter how much I toss and turn, I decided to get up, turn on the electric light, and elaborate a little more.

It is likely that when Buddhism was introduced to China, Confucian scholars and Taoist believers alike looked down upon it. The main reason was that the Buddha was not of "Yellow descent"—and certainly not a descendant of Chi You. Since it was not a product of the Central Plains, it was inevitably a foreign religion and should not be promoted.

One person known to oppose Buddhism from a Confucian-Taoist standpoint is Han Yu. This is, of course, because he suffered greatly from it, making a name for himself in the process. However, his theories became well-known to later generations mainly because he was skilled in writing classical prose, which was considered "worthy of emulation" and widely circulated. In reality, by Han Yu's time, the mixture of Confucianism, Taoism, and Zen Buddhism had already transitioned from a formal to a psychological level, deeply rooted. The great success of the "Three Religions, One Source" theory is indicative of this.

Buddhism was able to gain prominence in China because it managed to capture the faith of several emperors. As for the reason it mixed with Confucianism and Taoism, I speculate that it was due to the advocacy of those ministers. Having read a few volumes of Confucian books, they never forgot that they were disciples of the sages, but they did not want to overtly defy the emperor's will. Therefore, they adopted a Confucian exterior with a Zen heart, neither monks nor laymen, creating the notion of "Three Religions, One Source" and "Buddhism and Confucianism are the same," which was essentially a self-deception. By the late Han and early Jin dynasties, Mouzi's *Treatise on Dispelling Confusion* and Sun Chuo's *Essay on Explaining the Way* both advocated the consistency of Buddhist and Confucian thought. *Essay on Explaining the Way* states:

"Zhou and Confucius are the Buddha, and the Buddha is Zhou and Confucius, merely different names for the inner and outer. ... Buddha, in Sanskrit, means 'awakened,' and in the Jin dynasty, it was interpreted as 'enlightened.' Meng Ke considered sages to be those who are first to awaken, and the meaning is the same. Zhou and Confucius rectified the evils of the time, while Buddhism only clarifies the root. They focus on the beginning and the end, but their ultimate goals are not different. Therefore, those who seek discord often see duality, while those who understand harmony find unity in everything."

From this, it is clear that the mixture of Buddhism and Confucianism was flawed and confused from the very beginning. The peacemaker's painstaking efforts are evident here.

Since the Jin Dynasty, due to the turbulent times, scholars and officials who had read the books of Confucius and Mencius became increasingly passive. As a result, the theory that "Buddha is Zhou and Confucius" further developed. Wearing Confucian robes and carrying prayer beads became fashionable. Some even held the *Classic of Filial Piety* in their left hand and the *Smaller Perfection of Wisdom Sutra* in their right hand at the moment of death, to show that they had no bias toward either.

However, there were indeed people who doubted that Buddhism and Confucianism were necessarily consistent. For example, Qiao Wang Shangzhi said in a letter to Zhang Xin'an:

"Buddhism speaks of karmic retribution as if it were an echo, and the words of the sages are clear and frightening. However, from the ancient emperors to King Wen, King Wu, the Duke of Zhou, and Confucius, their decrees and instructions were all-encompassing, yet none of them described the three lifetimes or explicitly recounted karmic retribution. All the sages exhausted reason and fully understood their nature, illuminating the causes of things. Why would they bear to watch people drown without lending a hand, without even a single word to show them the path? Furthermore, they fished without nets, and their arrows did not target roosting birds. The finest and fattest were offered to God. From this perspective, it is difficult to understand..."

Later, Bo Yi of the Tang Dynasty also used the fact that "Buddhist teachings were not found in Chinese poetry and books" as a reason to reject Buddhism. Han Yu also said that the Buddha "does not speak the law of the former kings, does not wear the robes of the former kings, and does not know the righteousness of ruler and subject or the affection between father and son" as evidence that Buddhism and Confucianism were incompatible. However, despite the rejections, the idea that Buddhism and Confucianism were consistent still permeated everywhere. One can see in the notes of Tang and Song people that it was often recorded that a certain monk was a descendant of Wang Yishao or Xie Lingyun, proving that they had the potential to study. The prevailing trend at that time, although not to the point of removing one's Confucian hat to reveal a bald head, had already blended together in thought. Therefore, Song Confucian scholars rejected Buddhism but ended up "sitting on a Zen bed and cursing Zen," unknowingly influenced by its poison.

From the Yuan and Ming dynasties to modern times, although Buddhism seemed to have declined on the surface, in reality, Zen principles had infiltrated Confucianism and Taoism, and Buddhist teachings had permeated people's hearts. They had become one and the same, without leaving a trace. This is why those remnants of the old era, although having read Confucian classics and claiming to uphold tradition, mostly understand a little about Hinayana and Mahayana Buddhism. When unable to maneuver, they would quote profound principles and contemplate the emptiness of form, embracing a "live and let live" mentality, playing deaf and dumb, and drifting towards a confused death.

The Song Dynasty scholar Cheng Yi criticized the Buddhists, saying, "In the past, they deceived people by exploiting their ignorance, but now they deceive people by exploiting their intelligence." This is indeed true.

University Days (25) 198

— By German author Storm, translated by Chen Yin Zhi

Already with her foot on the edge of the boat, about to step aboard, she suddenly hesitated and turned to look at us. Those distinctive, exotic black eyes, I had seen before, but not for a long time. Now, they met my gaze, and I knew it was Lenore Poligar. She had grown up, and a hint of unambiguous maidenly blush appeared beneath her brown cheeks. But she still retained that peculiar, graceful, indolent air, which had unknowingly fascinated my childish heart. My heart boiled with emotion, almost completely forgetting those ladies beside me. Those black eyes seemed to look at me with a pleading expression. I heard the old female tailor urging her, and the boatman prompting her to board the boat without elegant words, but this slender brown girl still stood motionless, as if in a dream, turning her eyes to me.

As if propelled by an inexplicable natural force, I had already taken a few steps towards that ferry boat, but I suppressed myself. I thought of Christopher. His honest blue eyes seemed to suddenly appear before me. "That boat cannot accommodate all of us," I said to the ladies. Then, we walked along the coast to another ferryboat from the side. ——But I still looked back at Lenore once. She lowered her head to her chest and slowly walked across the deck into the bottom of the boat, which lay on the calm water under the golden light of the setting sun.

On the return trip, I sat next to the rudder, not saying much, and feeling very uneasy. My eyes were always fixed on that ferryboat moving far ahead. Those young ladies tried to engage me in conversation, but they were unsuccessful.

"Why are you so useless today!" one of them said, "That pretty seamstress of ours seems to have taken your soul away!"

"Is Lenore your seamstress?" I asked, perplexed.

"Lenore! How do you know her name is Lenore?"

"I grew up in the same town as her. My first 'Mazurka' was danced with her in dancing school."

"So that's how it is!—So some people say she still likes to dance with university students now."

Our conversation about Lenore ended there. But now I understand why Christopher was unwilling to say much about Lenore.

Later in the winter, I saw him walking with Lenore in public places several times, often accompanied by the lame Mary, and sometimes by an even older woman. I guessed she was the aunt who inherited the estate, who took his beloved away not long before the poor French tailor died.

Infuriating! 199

— By Long Gong Gong

One damp, chilly afternoon in early spring, I found myself painfully missing a distant friend. I wasn't sure if it was a flaw that this friend of mine knew how to sing the little song "The Merry Widow," but I urgently needed to hear it—that way, my memories would be clearer, and the separation between us would be shorter. So, I went to a movie theater to see a film with that song's name.

But there, I discovered something else.

Fumbling in the dark, talking loudly, two men and a woman came in. The woman was holding a small child, and the men were both wearing long gowns. I couldn't see their faces at all, but I sensed that they gave me a feeling of oppression. They were happy, comfortable, and free, as if they were sitting in their own living room.

The woman was in a very difficult situation. She tried various methods to quietly threaten and coax her child, trying to stop the constant noise. When her methods didn't work, she stood up and took the child outside to avoid the dissatisfaction of other audience members. She had to keep running in and out, so she was uneasy and busy.

The two men talked even more than their female companion, about doing business, watching the show, and the weather. Their conversations were short and quick, and they spoke so urgently that questions and answers seemed to come from the same person without interruption. There was no conflict, no difference of opinion. They first always said "good, good" to everything—based on this, I gradually imagined their faces and guessed that they were two small merchants.

"Is it better to watch a traditional opera or a movie...?"

"Quiet!" one person said like that, and the other person answered in the same way. The latter also offered an opinion:

"Is it better to watch a Chinese movie or a foreign movie...?"

"Refreshing!" The former also answered in the same tone.

They were talking very harmoniously, until Hebert was flirting with McDonald. This couple was sitting in a chair together, and Hebert was saying moving words of love to her. McDonald was then stimulated, her body uneasily moving in the seat, her face showing a confused, bewildered expression. For this matter, the two small merchants used regretful feelings and almost "pitying the fairer sex" to give their affirmative criticism:

"Infuriating!"

"Ah, infuriating!"

When a small businessman is shocked by his own talent, and is satisfied to find it, his vitality often develops to the highest limit, and reveals an astonishing obstinacy. In a few seconds, two college students next to them shouted at them to shut up, and they started arguing recklessly.

It was only at that time that I really felt very clearly that watching a movie was not an easy thing. Because of all kinds of restrictions and obstacles, it is difficult for people to understand each other, even face to face.

So, in the literary world, there have been cases of treating Laurel or Hardy as Chaplin, and saying all sorts of praises.

Agricultural Instructor 200

— By Xu Ying

That evening, our "Farmers' Tea Garden" was exceptionally crowded. Ever since Zhou Huzi gave me a "nail" this morning, word spread like wildfire. Everyone who knew about it made time to come to the tea garden to listen to my "lecture."

At 6:45, I arrived at the tea garden. Hundreds of eyes immediately focused on me. Talking, laughing, singing, shouting—everything automatically stopped. There was unprecedented order. I calmly walked in, and they politely made way for me. As I took my seat, I glanced around. Zhou Huzi was grinning, his face full of glee. Chen Laosan was squeezed into another corner, gesturing and talking in a low voice.

With ten minutes to go before the lecture, I sat in my seat and waited, sipping the tea that the waiter brought me. The tea garden, inside and out, was filled with a tense atmosphere. The air was very solemn, like an arrow on a bowstring, the bow fully drawn. I stole glances around, carefully observing the expressions. Some who sympathized with me looked rather sad, while those who usually disapproved of me looked somewhat triumphant.

At 7:00, the waiter rang the iron bell, ding-dang, ding-dang. I stood up and first asked, "Is Village Chief Chen here?"

Chen Laosan, hurriedly responded, buttoning his long gown as he squeezed out of the crowd. With his small head and balding pate, and tall figure, he bowed and nodded repeatedly to me, quickly walking to the lecture table.

"Village Chief Chen," I said with a smile, "Today is like two parties in a lawsuit. Please act as a judge. Brother Zhou is probably here too, so please let Brother Zhou report first. I'll save my words for last."

"Good, good, good," Chen Laosan, said anxiously, sweat streaming from his head as he fanned himself frequently with his small folding fan. "Brother Shang, Brother Zhou, come, you go first..."

Zhou Huzi stood up, smiling, his beard spreading like a flower. I remained in my seat, sipping my tea and listening to his report.

He spoke with animated gestures, his voice booming.

"This morning, Mr. Li was watching the workers plow the fields. I went over and said, 'You don't deserve to be an agricultural instructor! You're not as good as the farmers, how can you instruct them?' 'I'll show you how it's done. Let's have a contest. You plow one row, and I'll plow one row. Whoever plows straighter, deeper, and faster, will be the instructor!' Later, I won. Mr. Li said he would give me the agricultural instructor's position tonight. Neighbors, please be witnesses. We farmers can show you we're not useless!"

Zhou Huzi's tone was somewhat aggressive and overbearing. After speaking, he clasped his fists and smiled, bowing to the crowd. Immediately, a roar of "Good!" erupted from the crowd. It was noisy.

Chen Laosan's demeanor seemed a bit more imposing. Smiling again at me, he said, "Please, Mr. Li!"

The words I had prepared in my belly were unusable in this situation. I had to use a sword to block a spear, and an egg can never break a stone. I had to harden myself.

I got up from the bench and stepped onto the table. I stood firmly, not speaking at first, but scanning the entire crowd. At that moment, the sun was setting, and the room was filled with a magnificent golden-red light. Then, the crowd quieted down. There was no sound.

"Brother Zhou," I said, "You truly have great skill. I know that Brother Zhou is not only good at plowing, but he's also excellent at planting rice. I truly admire you. But—"

I said loudly, shouting it all in one breath—

"Does an agricultural instructor only need to know how to plant rice? Brother Zhou's wheat planting is not so good! Does he recognize the tree species in this area? Even less so! He doesn't know how to grow vegetables, his silkworm raising is sloppy, and he doesn't understand how to open up mountains! Do you want an instructor who only knows how to plow a straight row? If we're talking about plowing a straight row, everyone here, which one of you isn't like Brother Zhou, which one of you isn't stronger than me? He can do it, can't you do it?

"Think about it, who should be the instructor, him or me? Please tell me!"

I scanned the crowd again. No one spoke. Zhou Huzi's face suddenly changed, and he glared at me. I said, "Brother Zhou, I'm sorry, I'll let you have it another day."

After I finished speaking, I left, followed by a clamor. I paid no more attention to what they were saying.

Mosquitoes 201

— Chen Zizhan

Of all the small insects that especially breed in summer and are most annoying, none are more so than flies, bedbugs, and mosquitoes. Mosquitoes, though not as dirty as flies or as insidious as bedbugs, when they gather together, make a noise like thunder, disturbing people's sweet dreams at night, which is even more annoying than flies and bedbugs. I remember in the "Jin Lou Zi," it was said, "Duke Huan of Qi slept in a cypress chamber and said to Zhongfu, 'The white birds are buzzing; they must be hungry. Open the green gauze window and let them in.'" The white birds are mosquitoes, which is said in the "Great Ritual," Xia Xiaozheng. Apparently, using gauze curtains to keep out mosquitoes has been around for a long time. Duke Huan of Qi discussed letting a swarm of hungry mosquitoes fly into the green gauze window. This can be considered the intention of a benevolent man, though it may seem a bit pedantic. I also remember that the great poet Fan Chengda of the Southern Song Dynasty had a short poem titled "Suffering from Mosquitoes":

"White birds buzzing, suffering from hunger at night, unable to bear the smoke driving them out of the window. Small insects share my worries, daring to fly tirelessly, driven by hunger."

This "Grand Councilor Prime Minister," "admired by all officials, famous throughout the world," actually cared about the hunger of mosquitoes, quite opposed to killing mosquitoes. He even said, "Small insects share my worries," seemingly having such broad sympathy as "treating all people as brothers and all things as companions." I once shamelessly stole the meaning of his poem. A young lady who had been in prison told me that she had written a eulogy for sparrows in prison because a sparrow flew into the prison, couldn't find a way out, and died after hitting the wall. I was very moved when I heard this, so I wrote a short poem for her and gave it to her. The poem says:

"Ashamed to lodge a branch in the deep forest, resolutely flying to the controlled land, brave and sad. I should share your worries; not worship Gaotao, but worship the sparrow!"

This young lady said that I had a bit of a humanitarian spirit, but in fact, I don't know what is called an -ism. It is said that some humanitarians must protect even small lives like bedbugs and mosquitoes, such as the "Protecting Life Paintings" by the famous cartoonist Feng Zikai, but they forget about people. I am not like that; I love to catch bedbugs, love to swat flies, and love to smoke out mosquitoes. If frogs and turtles were really delicious, and I could get used to eating them, and couldn't eat bird's nest and shark fins, and couldn't eat chicken, duck, fish, and meat, then taking frogs and turtles to make up for it wouldn't be considered cruel and unkind. When I was young, I was extremely thin, truly "too weak to bear the weight of my clothes." The doctor said I had anemia, so I hated bedbugs and mosquitoes that sucked my blood the most. I was born in the western countryside of Changsha, where the villagers hate bedbugs the most. If a family has bedbugs, it is as shameful as a man being a thief and a woman being a prostitute. After I entered the city, I was still afraid of saying that there were bedbugs on my bed, and catching bedbugs was a daily task, but I wrote "Liu Fei" (catching bedbugs) on the daily schedule. Once, someone who knew a little about philology spread my "Liu Fei" as a joke. As for mosquitoes, there are too many in the countryside. In the summer evenings, they buzz everywhere. Sometimes when breathing quickly, mosquitoes would get stuck in the nostrils. Sometimes when opening my mouth to speak, mosquitoes would break into my throat. There are fewer mosquitoes in the city, but compared to Shanghai, Changsha is considered the place with the most mosquitoes. I remember in the "Biographies of Empresses and Consorts" in the "History of the Southern Dynasties," it was said that Lady Ding, the concubine of Emperor Wu of Liang, when she was young, spun thread with the neighboring girls under the moonlight. Those girls were pitifully bitten by mosquitoes, but only the concubine didn't feel it. Perhaps the mosquitoes knew she was a noble person, so they didn't bite her! The same book, "Biographies of Honest Officials," says that Chu Sunqian "was honest and clean in the two counties and five prefectures he served from youth to old age. He lived frugally, using only rough mats and screens. In winter, he had cloth quilts and reed mats; in summer, he had no gauze curtains, but he never had mosquitoes and gnats biting him at night, which many people found strange." Mosquitoes also knew to reward honesty, which cannot but be said to be a strange thing. However, we must not be too naive and trust people too much. We must know that what historians record cannot all be taken as true, not just the matter of mosquitoes not biting honest officials!

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Conversations

Short-Term Training Class for Prostitutes 202

— Chen

The newspaper recently reported a dispatch from Nanchang, saying: "The Popularization of Simple Education Association organized a short-term training class for prostitutes. The opening ceremony was held on the morning of the 13th. More than a hundred prostitutes attended, and each was given a copy of the 'Three Principles of the People Thousand-Character Text.' The instructors gave speeches, saying that they hoped that they would attend classes on time, and that they must know that without literacy, they would not understand etiquette and righteousness, and hoped that they would work hard to encourage themselves, etc."

Prostitution has become a superfluous thing accompanying modern society. Precisely because it is a "superfluous thing," the general public has mixed opinions about it. Many chapter-and-section regular customers spare no effort to waste words and ink, leaving their names under the flowers. In many places, businesses rely on this to maintain "market prosperity," and oppose the prohibition of prostitution. The authorities use "flower donations" as a source of government expenditure, making it difficult to act rashly. All of this is enough to show that this "superfluous thing" is not an easy problem to solve.

Recently, many people who are concerned about the world and people's hearts feel that prostitutes are things that mislead the common people and harm society. Therefore, there are "Movements to Eliminate Gambling and Prostitution" in various places. For a time, meetings were held, ribbons were cut, speeches were given, items were exhibited, bells were rung, and cannons were fired, which was quite a spectacle and very prosperous. Of course, this is "meritorious to society" and a good thing, and we raise our hands in support. If prostitution prevails, the trend of abduction will inevitably become widespread, trapping women in a miserable and dark life, which is the first crime. Countless people, young and old, indulge in licentiousness, wasting time and abandoning their careers, and their virtues decline day by day. In severe cases, they are disgraced, bankrupt, and lose their families, which is too numerous to list, which is the second crime. As for leading people to extravagance, and women's useful bodies competing to do "non-productive labor," which indirectly affects the country and society, it cannot but be said to be a pathological phenomenon. If this "movement" can "eliminate" it, it will be beneficial in every way, "for the country and for the people."

However, the problem is not so simple. The occurrence of prostitution is because many women have already lost the opportunity and skills to live. In the end, they have no choice but to sell their bodies. If you want to "eliminate" it, you must give them the opportunity and ability to live. I think the purpose of the Nanchang Popularization of Simple Education Association's opening of a short-term training class for prostitutes may also be here. Moreover, only in this way can the prostitutes trapped in misery and darkness benefit.

Mountain Walk 203

— You Qi

"We're leaving! Get up!"

The head porter shouted at the top of his lungs, from this end to that end, echoing a urging tune throughout this entire small town, in a chaotic manner.

This town isn't very big, sparsely populated with a hundred or so households. The entire journey from the east end to the west end of this long street can be completed in the blink of an eye.

Just this one heart-piercing crossroad, with two small paths leading to the fields. The street isn't wide, but it can accommodate a sedan chair carried by four people. As for the houses? Some are high, some are low. Tiled houses are rare. Of course, one cannot be too demanding in terms of architecture. The houses are so dark, emitting the smell of pig grease and dampness.

"Still not up? We're leaving!" The head porter, panting, shouted again.

The people living in the town are accustomed to getting up early. Strangers, attacking them, surrounding them, watching, pointing. Perhaps it's not common for our large group of travelers to pass through their town, I thought.

"Xiao Liu, Li Tou, get the poles, tie them up quickly, and leave first." The third porter also rushed over, giving such instructions, with blue veins popping on his forehead.

Hemp ropes, carrying poles, in a hurried mess, talking, with the mist covering this quiet field, on their faces, there was the weariness of being not yet awake.

"Is it ready? Brother Xiao Liu, let's go, take a couple of puffs first, never mind!"

"Let's not go, that's three hundred cash! I haven't had breakfast yet!"

"Not smoking? Then how will you be able to carry anything later!"

The situation flashed through Xiao Liu's mind a few times. Finally, he didn't say anything else, and followed him into a thatched house with a lantern hanging at the door.

"Half swallowing, half spitting, the taste is short; one inhale, one exhale, the smoke meaning is long."

A pair of red paper couplets was pasted on the rafters of the thatched hut. Perhaps the days had been too long, and the color had been stripped away, turning into a scorched yellow.

"The sun has climbed onto the hillside, and you're still not leaving, you bunch of turtles!"

The head porter was really angry, sweat flowing profusely, his face flushed red, and his already hoarse throat entered a deeper stage after several frantic shouts.

No matter how hot the weather, here, headscarves cannot be avoided. Because of his anxiety, he finally removed the headscarf from his head, and the heat was steaming like a pot on his head. Really, he couldn't shirk the responsibility of urging them, because the porters deliberately delayed at this daily determined station.

The bright red sun, so delicate, fell from the edge of the hillside into the low, small window, reflecting a little brilliance in the darkness. This was telling us that it was already late, and we all got up one by one, preparing to set off.

"Third porter, how many have left ahead?" Tie asked, brushing his teeth.

"Ten loads of luggage, eight flower basket poles, seventeen shoulder poles, and some are still tying up, the sedan chairs and sliding chairs are also ready." He smiled, the sun taking away its previous bright red, secretly looking at his purple-black face.

"Come on, get ready to go, let's have breakfast at Datianba." Porter Zhang shouted back and forth.

"Datianba, how far is it?" I asked.

"Cross the mountain peak of the watershed ahead, and it's another six li."

A group of people, noisy and disorderly, left the simple little town after a period of extreme commotion, and began to travel on the sheep-intestine-like mountain path.

Around them, so solemn, the waterfall flows so crisp, the secluded valley is so deep, the hillside, green, the flowing clouds, misty, farmers' songs, birds' songs, this melodious sound wave, showing the softness of the mountains.

The porters were accustomed to using jargon, answering each other in their jargon about how to avoid things.

"Green canopy sweeps the top, ah! (referring to mountain trees branches sweeping the head)"

"Raise the carrying pole over the ridge, ah!"

"Green grass flowers ahead, ah! (referring to horse manure)"

"A puddle of thin cba cha yo!"

...

In the long mountain path, the porters echoed vigilantly.

Melon and Plum Sketches 204

— Ji

It is already the height of summer: In the morning, a thick golden cloud floats on the horizon. A few birds sparsely make a couple of leisurely calls. This tone strikes into the nearly-awakened dream of people, like the sorrow of the strings on a dulcimer beyond the distant Guanshan mountains. It is so easy for people to recall the desolate circumstances beyond the border, and then, how quickly, to think of the flourishing big trees on the flower-like land of the South; On the branches perch many unknown birds, quietly using their pointed beaks to preen their feathers after waking up, occasionally chirping a couple of times, trying to use sounds similar to strings to narrate the poems of the joys and partings of last night's dreams ah.

Then, someone lightly marked a red line in the sky above the horizon near the clouds. This is to foretell what a good day this entire day will be! Thus: In an instant, streams of light like red gold bloomed at the mark of the scarlet line. This light, shining on the blue sky, from near to far, soon turned the vast sky into a bright mirror.

Page 22

Thus, over there, at the end of the horizon, on the distant eastern deserted beach, a fiery sun leaped up, followed by the entire earth also becoming warm from cool, from warm to slightly cooked, and from slightly cooked to boiling.

A new day has begun, a summer day ah.

The heat is ceaselessly strengthening, scorching the earth, urging its growth and progress. Afterwards, let the abundant autumn come as a reward for the effort of growth. But, even so, how much suffering must the creatures galloping on this baking land have! The sun has begun its post on the inspector's position. In the countryside, the farmers, men and women, and children, with half-full stomachs, a pair of tired eyes, and a feeling of weariness and resentment towards life itself; hunched over, pouting, resentfully heading towards the fields. There, they will use their sweat to moisten these broad, hard, dry, stubborn and ruthless lands, organizing them piece by piece, turning them over and harrowing them. Every year, they must first use the money and labor of their own children to guarantee the harvest of this year; But in these days, as known from past facts: these dry, stubborn and ruthless clods of earth are such a vague and unreliable kind of lender ah. In this fire-scorched summer, people cannot help but ask: Sweat is dripping onto the ground drop by drop, but where is the reward for this labor, and what can be used to guarantee it?

In the small towns, after the Dragon Boat Festival, in the heart of summer, it is precisely the busy farming season. The shops and teahouses are all in a period of "clearing out." The streets are sparse. The shopkeepers open their doors, only staring blankly at the empty streets. The sun shines, and the eternally uneven cobblestone road already seems to be boiling with fire. The shop assistants are idle, dozing off on the counters in twos and threes, and some lean half their bodies and chat with the familiar "bachelors" on the street. The teahouse is equally deserted. Apart from a few "old gentlemen" from the city, few people come to town to buy a pot of tea or sit for a while to chat with someone. Summer is an exciting season. After the sun has boiled the earth, it also stirs up the entire biological world. People, along with other animals, abandon everything in this season most suitable for growth and become busy, letting the birds call and letting the wind blow. It is necessary to put aside comfort and save it for the future, flowing with the sweat of labor. At this time, leisure is inappropriate, and laziness is inappropriate; Summer requires people to labor, to sweat, and not to lie on a bamboo couch and have people bring "plums and watermelons" ah.

George Bernard Shaw Advocates Interracial Marriage between Blacks and Whites 205

— Te

Aren't black people generally regarded by many as an inferior race in the world? But things are unexpected, and the world-renowned British writer George Bernard Shaw, recently returned from a trip to South Africa, actually advocates interracial marriage between black and white residents in Africa. According to his opinion, only this method can the white people of South Africa solve the important problems on which their survival depends. Shaw also explained that black people are by no means an inferior race. Shaw's ability to eliminate ethnic boundaries and break class concepts is certainly worthy of admiration. But what Shaw is doing is still for the survival of the white people of South Africa. After the white race breeds, where is there room for the black race to survive? Shaw also said that Africa ultimately belongs to the African people, not to many competing powers, which is a very vague view. Once the land is occupied by a different race, it is more difficult to restore it than climbing to heaven. Moreover, the same race always protects the white race, as we can see in the dispute between Italy and Abyssinia now. The Abyssinian government recently sent a telegram to the US government, applying for the invocation of the Kellogg-Briand Pact to prevent Italy from starting a war. The US replied with empty words, and recently six countries, France, Britain, Belgium, Czech Republic, Sweden, and Denmark, banned the transportation of military supplies to Abyssinia. If the war between Italy and Abyssinia breaks out, Abyssinia's armaments, not only can't match Italy's rice, but also have no rear supply, then defeat is inevitable. But although Italy intends to use the power of thunder to add to Abyssinia, Abyssinia has never shown a sign of surrender. Shaw's statement that black people are not an inferior race is certainly justified. People with this kind of spirit will never perish in the world.

A few hours after Shaw returned to London from South Africa, he spoke to a reporter from the Daily Telegraph who came to interview him about what he considered a serious matter. He was greatly impressed by the very good climate of South Africa. But what caused the danger was that terrible sunlight.

"The problem," he said, "is whether white people can survive in these places, and now it is gradually becoming serious. I am not saying that you will die because you are not acclimatized; you will not die. The problem is whether your descendants can be born in South Africa. When I was in South Africa, I encountered a rather surprising thing, which was that the railway tycoon Bill Row pleaded with white people to immigrate to South Africa and maintain the white population there. What does that mean? The public sees that the white race in America is very rich, and thinks it is not difficult to fill South Africa with white people, but South Africa will not be filled. This is not a birth control problem, because many people in South Africa are very willing to have children, but they cannot make them grow up. I think this may be because the sunlight in South Africa is too strong and not suitable for people with white skin. The remedy is probably only to make the skin black. That is to say, the white people in South Africa may as well marry black women."

"Wouldn't your old ideal provoke the hatred of white people?" the reporter asked:

"That's right," Shaw replied, "but there are already many mixed races in the world now. I heard smart people in Hawaii say that the natives of the South Pacific islands are gradually disappearing. Purebred people rarely remain. Mixing the two colors in South Africa may solve the problem. It must be known that this is not a black and white problem. The first thing to know is that there is no such thing as a white race on the face of the earth. The Chinese call us red-haired people, which is correct. The Zulu people of Africa are indeed a noble race. In the past, many people tried to bring them down to an inferior position, but the result was always failure, because they are not an inferior race. If you see them working, you will definitely want British workers to work like them."

Shaw also thought that this problem was not limited to South Africa, but could also be extended to a large part of the African continent.

Shaw continued: "I often say that the old German colonies should be returned to Germany, and Mussolini is also trying to extend his hand to Abyssinia. Although you can now divide Africa among the European powers, one day the African people will say to you, 'None of you are allowed to occupy the land of Africa'! At that time, the people of Africa, whether they are natives, white people, black people, or whatever, will see that Africa ultimately belongs to the African people, not to many competing European powers. Bloodlines can be mixed, but the natives of Africa have their special abilities, and in the long run, we can see that only they have the ability to survive in Africa, and no one else does.

Its story describes a infatuated composer pursuing a female lead in his new work. Although the woman also loves him, her attitude is always aloof and indifferent, expressing nothing. The composer leaves in anger. At this time, the premiere date of the new play is approaching, and the important scores have not been written yet, but he doesn't care, making the director jump with anxiety. Shen Bao Local Supplement Automotive Weekly

Renault Cars Cause a Sensation in Shanghai 214

— Fu

Three Wonderful Styles to Suit All Needs

The amazing progress in the automotive industry in the past two years can be seen in the 1935 Renault cars. Whether it is the application of the principle of aircraft aerodynamics to the car body and structure, or the engine construction that meets the principle of economy everywhere, Renault is the most worthy of praise. The various advancements that Renault has in all aspects are too numerous to mention, but its price has not increased at all, and its internal spaciousness and comfort have not been diminished. This is especially commendable and is truly a major success in mechanical engineering.

The new Renault cars have three groups in total. The beauty of their paint and the magnificence of their appearance have caused a sensation in Shanghai and are the vehicles that people in the automotive industry unanimously admire. The new cars have a complete range of styles, which can be used for all purposes, whether it is for office, sports, or family, and they are extremely pleasant and competent. The appearance of the new cars is extremely beautiful and moving, but their content is excellent and outstanding. Renault has always been known for its magnificent performance, and this is why Renault car owners have always been extremely satisfied. Now, the car not only maintains these advantages, but also promotes them even more.

Among the various styles of Renault, the Vivas Stella sports style is the most attractive. Its construction is based on actual aircraft testing, so it can definitely meet the principle of aircraft aerodynamics. Its stored power, beautiful and magnificent appearance, and unattainable speed are the characteristics that first give people a deep impression. As for its internal position, it is more spacious, and the paint decoration is extremely beautiful. This new car has three styles: convertible coupe, two-door sedan, and enlarged van. The van has five seats, which are extremely comfortable. In addition, the Vivas Stella family van has two types: five-seater and seven-seater. The front and rear seats are spacious and can be stretched at will. The seven-seater is equipped with six windows, all equipped with a windless ventilation system. Another style is a sports car with a sporty appearance. Its performance is almost the same as that of the large sports style, but its consumption is more economical. For those who want to drive quickly in the city, this vehicle is especially suitable because of its unusually sensitive acceleration rate and extremely easy handling, which is especially suitable for the vehicle traffic conditions in this city. The parking space it occupies is smaller than usual. The car body is particularly beautiful and magnificent. According to this new type of Renault car, one of its most significant advances is the automatic starter and the new carburetor. The reason why the new car can be started immediately in any weather is that it has this new equipment. The Renault engine adopts a special suspension method, so it can ensure that no slight vibration occurs. As for the wheels, they are extremely easy to replace without any effort. The spare wheel is placed in a concealed place, and the position is just right, so it does not hinder the streamline shape of the entire car at all. Furthermore, if the general car owners also consider others, they will definitely praise another equipment of Renault. According to this equipment, there is nothing else, that is, the rear direction indicator that allows vehicles behind to see the direction of the car.

Types and Descriptions of Car Brakes and Brakes 215

— Zhenmin

The main components that control every car are the brakes and the brakes. If the car does not have a brake device, then the car cannot run. If the car does not have a brake device, then the car will keep running and cause various damages. These two machines are indispensable. In recent years, there has been an increasing trend in the improvement of automobile engineering and manufacturing, especially in the improvement of brakes and brakes, which has increased the braking efficiency to more than 90%. Therefore, the new modern cars only need very little force to trigger the engine to run, or to suddenly stop the high-speed engine in a few seconds. These are all very obvious examples.

There are many types of brakes and brakes, especially because of the prosperity of electricity in recent years. New machines are constantly being introduced, while old brakes or brakes are constantly being eliminated. Now, the most important types are listed below.

A. Braking Machines

(1) Heat Pipe Brake The earliest brake used. It uses external heat—usually gas media—to increase the temperature of the compressed air in the cylinder to the combustion point. Finally, an explosion occurs in the cylinder, causing the piston to push the crank, and then push the propeller to make the car body move forward. Although the ignition of this system is stable, the explosion time in the cylinder is not fixed. This is a very big shortcoming, and it also requires a large amount of combustion gas for ignition. This is enough to increase the price of fuel, so new cars rarely use this braking system now.

(2) Natural Combustion Ignition Brake This brake does not use external heat to increase the temperature of the gas in the cylinder. It completely uses the volume compression of the gas mixture to increase the temperature to the combustion point, causing the gas in the cylinder to explode to push the piston. This gas mixture is limited to a certain medium-sized oil mixed with air. Highly volatile oils, such as gasoline, etc., cannot be used. Therefore, only 1 or 2 percent of cars now use this brake.

(3) Electric Brake 95 out of every 100 cars now use electric brakes. Because this brake has extremely high efficiency and the time is very fast. It can push the car body in two or three seconds, which is really unmatched by any brake. Their functions all use the principle of induction electricity and appropriate machinery. They can also be divided into the following two types. A, Switch System (—Make-ander-Bak System)—This system is the most widely used. It uses the induction effect of the first and second coils to generate induction current. The first coil is equipped with a switch, which uses a cam and electromagnetic action to connect and disconnect the switch from time to time. As a result, an induced voltage is generated in the coil, causing sparks between the poles. The occurrence of this spark is inside the cylinder, so the temperature of the gasoline and air mixture in the cylinder is increased to a considerable extent, causing an explosion, which pushes the piston and makes the car body move forward. The speed and sensitivity of this braking are really unforeseen by any engineer. B, Jump-Spark System—The difference between this system and the previous one lies in the arrangement of the electrodes and the level of the voltage. The electrodes in method (A) are movable and the voltage is also very low. The current system is just the opposite. There are two fixed electrodes in the cylinder, with a small gap between them, and the rotation of the cam is used to suddenly increase the induced electricity in the coil. As a result, high-voltage sparks occur between the two poles, jumping into the gap and suddenly increasing the temperature of the gas in the cylinder, and the volume increases accordingly, causing the piston to move forward and the wheels to rotate. Because the voltage of this system is very high, capacitors are often installed to prevent excessive voltage and prevent the danger of short circuits. Although the two methods (A) and (B) are roughly similar, method (A) is much simpler than method (B) and there is no short circuit or other phenomena. Therefore, method (A) is used in most new cars now. Now that we have explained the brake in detail, we will now analyze the general types of brakes as follows.

B Mechanism Braking Machines

(1) Mechanical Motor Mechanical braking is the simplest. It uses the leverage effect to make the "brake shoe" (brake shoe is usually made of rubber or steel) tightly attached to the rear wheel. Due to the friction force, the rear wheel is stopped from moving forward. The biggest benefit of this system is that it is simple and easy to repair. However, steel or iron brake shoes are prone to rust, which makes the braking force unbalanced and loses its efficiency. Therefore, it is rarely used on new cars.

(2) Hydraulic Brake It uses the distribution of hydraulic force to brake the wheels. Usually, two connected vertical cylinders (with a large and a small cross-sectional area) are used instead of levers. The cylinder is filled with water or light oil. When braking, you only need to lightly step on the footboard to make the brake shoe connected to the large cylinder tightly attached to the wheel, so that the car body stops moving forward. The braking efficiency produced by this method is ten times that of the first method. However, the biggest drawback is that the cylinder is very prone to leakage. Not only does the efficiency disappear, but repairs are also difficult. It is more widely used than method (1).

(3) Air Brake The structure of this brake is exactly the same as that of the hydraulic brake. The only difference is that the cylinder is filled with air. This can avoid the danger of leakage. Before the air is used for braking, it is first compressed by a motor and stored in a cylinder. When applied, the valve can be opened, and the high-pressure air rushes into another cylinder, so that the "brake shoe" is tightly attached to the wheel and the car body stops moving forward. This compressed air can be continuously transported by a small motor. When the brake is not in use, the small motor can automatically stop. This method is much more advanced than the previous two methods. Therefore, 60% of cars now use this brake.

(4) Electromagnetic Brake Like the brake, it also uses the induction electricity of the coil for braking. Its structure is quite simple. A fixed joint is installed on the main rotating shaft of the engine and rotates with the shaft. Another joint is tightly connected to the center of the induction coil with a small shaft. This induction coil is connected to a battery. When braking, you only need to turn on the circuit, and induction electricity will be generated in the coil, which will generate magnetic force. This will cause the small shaft of the joint to move forward. The two joints will automatically mesh, and the rotating shaft will stop running. Although this brake is not as efficient as the air brake, it is widely used now because of its simple structure.

Overall, although there are many types of brakes and brakes mentioned above, it is very obvious that electric power is gradually being used on cars to obtain highly efficient braking.
