Ford V8 Car Breaks Saigon to Inland River Record 216

Recently, Mr. Di Yuliang broke the record for the car race between Saigon and Hanoi again. The road between the two places is 1,732 kilometers long. It only took 19 hours and 59 minutes to arrive. The speed is equivalent to 86.6 kilometers or 53.7 miles per hour. Mr. Di Yuliang's previous record was 23 hours and 15 minutes. The record has been broken six times in the past few years, and five of them were broken by Ford cars. Mr. Di's engine cover was sealed this time, which makes it even more commendable. On the same day, Mr. Tao Nier also broke the previous record in 20 hours and 44 minutes. However, Mr. Di Yuliang started later and was able to beat Mr. Tao by a faster time of 45 minutes. However, Mr. Tao was still full of energy when he arrived at the finish line and said that if the car had not been delayed by trains and ferries, it would not have been difficult to achieve the same good time as Mr. Di.

Ten Horsepower Four-Cylinder Marius Encounters Danger in South Africa 217

— Fu

The Connock Automobile Company in South Africa recently received a letter from Mrs. Davis, the owner of a Marius car there, describing the dangers she encountered in South Africa and praising the sturdiness and beauty of the Marius car, which made her very satisfied. Now, the letter is translated as follows to inform the general public who are concerned about Marius cars.

"You may be honored to know about the small dangers we encountered on our way back to Babbotang. When we were driving about 30 miles and approaching Carolina, we saw three or five natives wandering in the road. The time was 9:30 in the evening, and it was already late at night. However, because we were riding in a ten-horsepower four-cylinder Marius, the excellence of its car lights is well known to you. Therefore, although it was pitch black all around at that time, we could see the natives very clearly from the car. As the car moved forward and got closer to the natives, they all jumped to the side of the car and shot. The bullets hit the front door of my car, but fortunately they did not penetrate. However, my knee was right in the center of the car door, and the car door was suddenly shaken by the bullets. My knee was also injured as a result. At that time, the sound of gunfire was like a string of beads, and we had no weapons, so we dared not stop. We still sped away. After we got out of the encirclement, we checked the place where the car was shot. The dents were deep enough to fit a finger, and the steel skin was peeling off. The power of the bullet can be imagined. If we were riding in the old car before, it can be said that the bullets would have pierced my knee. Now, because Marius is made of strong and solid high-quality materials, we were able to avoid this disaster. It is really a great fortune. In addition to the above-mentioned unfortunate incident, my ten-horsepower four-cylinder Marius has been used for more than a year. I have driven it in various weathers and on various rugged and bad roads. The good results have made me overjoyed and extremely satisfied. As for climbing mountains, its agility, ease of use, and its ability to stay cool are all outstanding and unmatched. In addition to my joy, I specially write to inform you."

The right is a group photo of colleagues from the Military Transportation Office of the Nanjing Military Commission after recently visiting the Madi Automobile Company.

Tires Still Intact After Being Submerged in Water for More Than Ten Years 218

A car that had been submerged in the Hudson River near New York City in the United States for more than ten years was recently salvaged. It was found that all four wheels were equipped with Goodyear rubber tires. The tires still contained air. The spokes were almost completely rusted, but the tires were still in good condition, and it seemed that they could still be used for driving. According to the product records of Goodyear Company, these four tires were made in 1921.
